Al-Ash'ari as Author and the Sunni Creedal Synthesis
Describes al-Ash'ari's role as author and the Sunni synthesis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the role of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an author who formulated the rational and theological system for the Sunni school, and the intellectual context of his mission.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari built a rational system that united the Sunni community against theological distortions.

In this opening passage, the author introduces Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as more than a mere author—he was the architect of a new rational framework for Sunni Islam. We learn that his work was not a personal project but a synthesis representing the diverse Sunni milieu, from hadith scholars to moderate Hanbalis. This lesson covers his role and the broader Sunni context he aimed to defend.

Guided Path
1
Understand al-Ash'ari's self-conception
Read the passage to see that al-Ash'ari saw himself as laying a new intellectual foundation, not creating a personal school.
2
Identify the Sunni groups represented
List the groups mentioned: hadith scholars, Qur'an reciters, Sufis, moderate Hanbalis, followers of the four schools.
3
Recognize the purpose of his work
He aimed to complete the creedal aspect of the Sunni school in defense against distortions from Mu'tazilism and extremism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أ- أبو الحسن الأشعري مؤلفًا : كان إمامنا -رضي الله عنه- مؤلفًا، وصاحب قلم. وكان يُدرِك كما يشعر كلُّ من يقرؤه - أنه يضع أساس بناء عقليّ جديد، ليس مذهبًا لنفسه، أو نزعةً فكرية ذاتية : بل هو الصياغة العقلية، والصناعة الكلامية والنسق الفكري لموقف أو إن شئت لمذهب أهل السنة والجماعة؛ من المحدثين والقراء، وصوفية السلوك والاستقامة، ومعتدلي الحنابلة، وغيرهم من أتباع المذاهب الأربعة التي سادت الوسط السني، وتلقَّتْها الأمة بالقبول في المجال الفقهي العملي، وجاء هو ليكمل البناء، لهذا الموقف - أو المذهب السني – من الجانب الاعتقادي ؛ انتصارًا لأحكام الكتاب والسنة ، التي شوشت عليها نزعاتُ الاعتزال والغلو، والخروج عن الجماعة ،والتشيع بالرغم من جهود الإمام أبي حنيفة النعمان (١٥٠هـ) صاحب الفقه الأكبر ورسالة العالم والمتعلم وغيرهما؛ بحيث يعتبره بعض الباحثين واضع علم الكلام، لكن جهوده بقيت مؤثرة في المجال الحنفي خاصة، وما قام به الشافعي وأحمد رضي الله عنهما- في مقاومة المبتدعين . وقد فعل الأشعري ذلك، لما انقدح في ذهنِهِ، واستقر في قلبه خلال تطور فكري طويل المدى، لا كما تصوّره الحكايات الرمزية ، من الرؤى المنامية والاعتكاف والخلوة لأسبوعين أو ثلاثة، ثم يخرج على الناس بمؤلفات جديدة، وموقف فكري متسق ومتكامل ، وهو المفكر المعروف خلال أعوام، بل عقود، سابقة في الوسط الاعتزالي ؛ مرتبطا بأكبر دعاته حينئذ، وهو الجبائي الكبير، محمد ابن عبد الوهاب - نقول : لقد انقدح في ذهنه، واستقر في وعيه، في منتصف العقد الأخير من القرن الثالث الهجري، وقد قارب عمره الأربعين - أمران : الأمر الأول: استحسان الخوض في علم كلام سُنّي جديد؛ فأصدر كتابه بهذا العنوان الذي يتطابق محتواه مع كتابه الآخر المقطوع بنسبته إليه، وهو : الحث على البحث، وليس كتاب الاستحسان إلا صياغة
A- Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari as an author: Our Imam - may Allah be pleased with him - was an author and a writer. He realized, as anyone who reads him feels, that he was laying the foundation of a new intellectual structure, not a personal school or a subjective intellectual tendency, but rather the rational formulation, the theological craft, and the intellectual system for the position - or if you will, the school - of Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama'ah: from the hadith scholars and Qur'an reciters, the Sufis of conduct and uprightness, the moderate Hanbalis, and others from the followers of the four schools that prevailed in the Sunni milieu and were accepted by the ummah in the practical jurisprudential field. He came to complete the building of this position - or the Sunni school - from the creedal side, in support of the rulings of the Book and the Sunnah, which had been disturbed by the tendencies of Mu'tazilism, extremism, dissension from the community, and Shi'ism, despite the efforts of Imam Abu Hanifah al-Nu'man (150 AH), the author of al-Fiqh al-Akbar and Risalah al-'Alim wa al-Muta'allim and others, such that some researchers consider him the founder of 'ilm al-kalam, but his efforts remained influential in the Hanafi field especially, and what al-Shafi'i and Ahmad - may Allah be pleased with them - did in resisting the innovators. And al-Ash'ari did that, because there became clear in his mind and settled in his heart during a long-term intellectual development - not as the symbolic stories imagine, from dream visions and seclusion for two or three weeks, then he emerges to people with new works and a consistent and integrated intellectual position, while he was a known thinker for years, rather decades, previously in the Mu'tazili milieu, associated with its greatest caller at that time, al-Jubba'i the elder, Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahhab - we say: there became clear in his mind and settled in his consciousness, in the middle of the last decade of the third century AH, when he was approaching forty, two matters: The first matter: approval of engaging in a new Sunni 'ilm al-kalam; so he issued a book with this title whose content matches his other book whose attribution to him is certain, which is: al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth, and the book al-Istihsan is nothing but a formulation
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction discussing Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's role as an author and the intellectual context behind his work. It begins by affirming that al-Ash'ari was indeed an author and a writer, and that readers can perceive that he was laying the foundation of a new rational structure. This structure was not a personal or subjective school, but rather the rational formulation, theological craft, and intellectual system of the Sunni position, representing various groups: hadith scholars, Qur'an reciters, Sufis, moderate Hanbalis, and followers of the four legal schools. Al-Ash'ari came to complete the creedal aspect of this Sunni position in defense of the Qur'an and Sunnah against distortions from Mu'tazilism, extremism, sectarianism, and Shi'ism. The passage notes that earlier efforts by Abu Hanifah (considered by some the founder of kalam) were influential mainly in Hanafi circles, and that al-Shafi'i and Ahmad also fought innovators. Then it explains that al-Ash'ari's change was the result of a long intellectual development, not sudden dreams or retreats. He had been a known figure in the Mu'tazili school for decades, associated with al-Jubba'i. In his late thirties (around 290 AH), two matters became clear to him: first, the approval of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, leading him to write a book titled 'al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' (Encouragement of Inquiry), and that the book 'al-Istihsan' is essentially a formulation of that encouragement.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari aim to complete with his work according to the passage?
A) The legal rulings of the four schools
B) The creedal aspect of the Sunni school
C) The methodology of hadith criticism
D) The Sufi path of spiritual purification

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's authorship was a collective effort to articulate the Sunni creed rationally, building on earlier legal foundations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content to passively inherit your creed, or do you actively engage with it as a rational system that requires your personal understanding and defense, as al-Ash'ari did?
?
In what ways do you allow personal preferences or intellectual trends to shape your understanding of Islam, rather than submitting to the collective Sunni tradition that al-Ash'ari worked to articulate?
?
Do you see yourself as a builder of the Sunni synthesis in your own context, or do you neglect the intellectual dimension of faith, leaving the defense of orthodoxy to others?

Al-Ash'ari's Intellectual Journey and the Call to Sunni Kalam
Explains al-Ash'ari's intellectual development and the two matters

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the long intellectual development that led al-Ash'ari to adopt Sunni kalam, and the two key matters that emerged in his thinking.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's turn to Sunni kalam was a gradual intellectual process, not a sudden conversion.

The passage continues by explaining that al-Ash'ari's shift was the result of a long-term intellectual evolution, contrary to popular symbolic stories. It reveals that in his late thirties, two matters became clear to him: the approval of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, and the publication of a book encouraging inquiry. This lesson examines that development.

Guided Path
1
Reject symbolic stories
Notice how the passage dismisses dream visions and short retreats as explanations for al-Ash'ari's change.
2
Identify the two matters
Find the two matters that became clear to al-Ash'ari: approval of Sunni kalam and the book encouraging inquiry.
3
Connect the books
Understand that al-Istihsan and al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth are essentially the same content.

The First Realization: Approval of Sunni Kalam
Editor details al-Ash'ari's first realization and its scholarly context.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first major realization that led al-Ash'ari to engage in Sunni kalam, including his book 'Al-Istihsan' and its relationship to his other works.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's first step was endorsing a new Sunni theology through rational inquiry, not abrupt conversion.

The editor of al-Luma' describes how al-Ash'ari's intellectual development was gradual. Two key matters crystallized in his mind around the age of forty. The first was his approval of engaging in a new Sunni theological science, which he called 'al-Istihsan' (approval). This lesson explores that first realization, its background, and its significance in his scholarly output.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the first realization
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Notice how the editor contrasts the gradual development with symbolic stories.
Pay attention to the phrase 'laisa kama tatawwarih al-hikayat al-ramziyya'.
2
Identify the key books mentioned
Find the titles: 'Al-Istihsan', 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth', and 'Al-Luma'. Understand the editor's claim about their relationship.
The editor asserts that 'Al-Istihsan' is a reformulation of 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth'.
3
Understand the refutation of a common misconception
The editor refutes attempts to reduce al-Ash'ari's work to only 'Al-Ibana'. Note the groups involved and the argument.
This shows that al-Ash'ari actively practiced rational kalam.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this first realization was crucial for al-Ash'ari's intellectual turn. How does it set the stage for his later works?

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة التحقيق
وقد فعل الأشعري ذلك، لما انقدح في ذهنه، واستقر في قلبه خلال تطور فكري طويل المدى، لا كما تصوره الحكايات الرمزية ، من الرؤى المنامية والاعتكاف والخلوة لأسبوعين أو ثلاثة، ثم يخرج على الناس بمؤلفات جديدة، وموقف فكري متسق ومتكامل ، وهو المفكر المعروف خلال أعوام، بل عقود، سابقة في الوسط الاعتزالي ؛ مرتبطا بأكبر دعاته حينئذ، وهو الجبائي الكبير، محمد ابن عبد الوهاب - نقول : لقد انقدح في ذهنه، واستقر في وعيه، في منتصف العقد الأخير من القرن الثالث الهجري، وقد قارب عمره الأربعين - أمران :
الأمر الأول: استحسان الخوض في علم كلام سني جديد؛ فأصدر كتابه بهذا العنوان الذي يتطابق محتواه مع كتابه الآخر المقطوع بنسبته إليه، وهو : الحث على البحث » (۱) ، وليس كتاب «الاستحسان» إلا صياغة أخرى، أو إصدارة جديدة لكتاب الحث على البحث، كما يظهر جليًا لمن يقوم بالمقارنة الدقيقة بينهما ، كما أن مؤلفاته الأخرى ومنها النص الذي بين أيدينا ؛ كتاب «اللمع»، وهو ثابت النسبة بلا ريب كما سنبين في موضع آخر (۱) ، مما يثبت أن محاولة كل من المعتزلة والظاهرية وغلاة الحنابلة، ومن وافقهم من بعض المستشرقين والباحثين العرب المعاصرين (۲) - ومؤسس هذه النظرية هو المستشرق المعروف باتجاهاته الخاصة «جولد تسيهر»، هذا لاختزال الشيخ في الإبانة دون سائر كتبه- لا جدوى منها في الصدد؛ لأنه في العديد من مؤلفاته، لا يقرر استحسان الكلام العقلي في أبواب العقيدة فحسب، بل يمارسه فعلا، ويؤلف فيه وفي أساليب الجدل، وطرق النظر على هذا الأساس، المبين في الاستحسان»، وهو المناظر المحترف، ولكنه الآن يناظر دفاعا عن موقفه السني الجديد . والأمر الآخر : أنه قد استقر في وعيه - أيضا - وجوب الرصد والتصدي لما ظهر في الحياة العقلية الإسلامية، من نزعات مادية، ويتطابق أيضًا مع ما يرد في أبواب النظر، والمعارف والجدل من كتاب اللمع) المقطوع بصحة نسبته إليه .
Introduction to the critical edition. And al-Ash'ari did that, because it became clear in his mind and settled in his heart through a long-term intellectual development, not as the symbolic stories portray: from dream visions and seclusion and retreat for two or three weeks, then he goes out to people with new writings and a consistent and integrated intellectual position, while he was the known intellectual during years, even decades, earlier in the Mu'tazilite milieu, connected to its greatest proponent at the time, al-Jubba'i the Great, Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Wahhab. We say: It became clear in his mind and settled in his consciousness, in the middle of the last decade of the third century AH, when he approached his fortieth year — two matters: The first matter: the approval of engaging in a new Sunni theological science; so he issued his book with this title whose content matches his other book whose attribution to him is certain, namely: 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' (1), and the book 'Al-Istihsan' is only another formulation, or a new edition of the book 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth', as appears clearly to one who makes a precise comparison between them. Also, his other works, including the text before us, the book 'Al-Luma', which is certainly attributed to him without doubt as we will show elsewhere (1), prove that the attempt of the Mu'tazilites, the Zahirites, the extreme Hanbalites, and those who agree with them among some Orientalists and contemporary Arab researchers (2) — and the founder of this theory is the well-known Orientalist with his particular tendencies, 'Goldziher' — to reduce the Shaykh to ['Al-Ibana'] to the exclusion of his other books — is futile in this regard; because in many of his writings he does not only affirm the approval of rational theological speech in the chapters of creed, but he actually practices it, and composes concerning it and concerning the methods of debate and ways of inquiry on this basis, explained in 'Al-Istihsan'; and he is the professional disputant, but now he disputes in defense of his new Sunni position. And the other matter: that it also settled in his consciousness — the necessity of monitoring and confronting what appeared in Islamic intellectual life of materialistic tendencies, and it also matches what appears in the chapters of inquiry, knowledge, and debate from the book 'Al-Luma' which is certainly attributed to him.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is an editor's explanation of the intellectual journey of Imam al-Ash'ari and two key realizations that shaped his later works. The editor begins by emphasizing that Ash'ari's shift from Mu'tazilism to Sunni theology was a gradual, long-term intellectual development, contrary to popular symbolic stories that depict it as a sudden conversion through dreams or a short retreat. Ash'ari had been a prominent figure in the Mu'tazilite school, closely associated with its leader al-Jubba'i. Then, around his fortieth year, two matters crystallized in his mind. The first was the approval (istihsan) of engaging in a new Sunni kalam, which led him to write a book on that topic. The editor notes that this book's content matches another work, 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth', and that 'Al-Istihsan' is essentially a reformulation of it. He also asserts that Ash'ari's other works, including the present book 'Al-Luma', are definitively attributed to him. This is used to refute attempts by various groups—Mu'tazilites, Zahirites, extreme Hanbalites, and some modern scholars—to reduce Ash'ari's legacy to only his book 'Al-Ibana', ignoring his numerous other works. The editor argues that Ash'ari not only endorsed rational kalam but actively practiced it and authored works on debate and inquiry. The second matter was the necessity of monitoring and confronting materialistic tendencies in Islamic intellectual life, which aligns with the themes in 'Al-Luma' regarding inquiry, knowledge, and debate.

Key Terms
استحسان الخوض في علم الكلام
الحث على البحث
الاستحسان
الإبانة
اللمع
الاعتزال
الجبائي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari's conversion was sudden and emotional, and his only significant work is 'Al-Ibana'.
Correction: The editor shows his conversion was gradual, and he authored multiple works including 'Al-Luma', 'Al-Istihsan', and others where he actively engaged in Sunni kalam.

Checkpoint
What does the editor say about al-Ash'ari's book 'Al-Istihsan' in relation to 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth'?
A) It is a completely different work.
B) It is a revised edition or reformulation.
C) It was written before al-Ibana.
D) It was written by al-Jubba'i.

Key Takeaway
The first matter settled in al-Ash'ari's mind was his approval of engaging in Sunni kalam, which he then encouraged and practiced in his writings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari's shift came after years of close association with the Mu'tazilites. What intellectual or spiritual attachments have you formed that might be holding you back from a deeper truth? Are you willing to endure a long, uncomfortable reassessment to align your convictions with what is right?
?
The editor contrasts the tidy story of a sudden conversion with the messy reality of gradual development. Which areas of your faith do you prefer to keep in a neat, oversimplified story? What would it cost you to honestly face the complexity of your own spiritual journey?
?
Al-Ash'ari did not abandon reason when he embraced Sunni theology; he repurposed it. Where in your life have you silenced your intellect because it challenged comfortable beliefs? Will you commit this week to examine one belief you hold through patient, honest inquiry, trusting that truth can withstand scrutiny?

The Second Realization: Confronting Materialistic Tendencies
Editor states al-Ash'ari's second realization: the necessity of confronting materialism.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second major realization that settled in al-Ash'ari's mind: the necessity of monitoring and confronting materialistic tendencies in Islamic intellectual life.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's second key insight was the need to actively counter materialistic ideas in Islamic thought.

Having approved of Sunni kalam, al-Ash'ari's consciousness also settled on another crucial matter: the obligation to monitor and confront materialistic tendencies that had emerged in Islamic intellectual circles. This lesson examines that second realization and its connection to his book 'Al-Luma'.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the second matter
Read the short Arabic passage and its translation. Note the wording: 'wujub al-rasd wa al-tasaddi'.
This realization is about active engagement against materialism.
2
Connect to al-Luma
The editor notes that this matter matches the content of 'Al-Luma' regarding inquiry and debate. Reflect on how this theme appears in the book.
Consider the broader context of early Islamic intellectual debates, such as those with skeptics and materialists.
3
Reflect on the significance for Ash'ari's approach
This second realization shows that al-Ash'ari's new Sunni commitment was not just theoretical but had a practical apologetic dimension.
He was a professional disputant now defending Sunni Islam.

Ash'ari's Dual Talent: Orator and Prolific Author
Refutes claim that al-Ash'ari was not an author.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how a common biographical claim about al-Ash'ari being only an orator is refuted by evidence of his extensive writings.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari authored hundreds of works, not just debated orally.

This passage tackles a specific biographical claim: that al-Ash'ari was a skilled debater but not an author, while his teacher al-Jubba'i was the opposite. The author of this introduction forcefully refutes that notion by pointing to al-Ash'ari's prolific written output, attested by himself and his students. This lesson unpacks that refutation and its supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the structure: it begins by presenting the claim, then refutes it with evidence.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the claim and refutation
Identify the claim made by some biographers and then the author's response. The claim is about al-Jubba'i and al-Ash'ari's different skills.
3
Examine the evidence presented
The refutation relies on the number of al-Ash'ari's works (hundreds) and the testimony of his students and later scholars. List the names mentioned.
They include Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, and al-Juwayni.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this refutation matters. It shows al-Ash'ari was not just an orator but a systematic thinker who left a substantial written legacy.
This corrects a potential misunderstanding about his scholarly output.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما ما يقوله بعض من مؤرخيه من أن أستاذه الجبائي، كان ذا قلم وقدرة على التأليف، وليس له القدرة نفسها على المناقشة والجدل، في المجالس المحتدمة حينذاك، في البصرة وبغداد، وكان تلميذه الشاب «أبو الحسن الأشعري ذا لسان وبيان ولا اشتغال له بالتأليف، فكان ينتدبه بدلا منه إذا دُعِيَ لهذه المجالس والمواجهات – فلئن صح ذلك بالنسبة للجبائي، فليس صحيحًا في حق رجل، تبلغ مؤلفاته المِئةَ أو المئات، وهي التي يعطينا قوائم بها في حياته، والتي ذكرها، وشرح بعضها، ولخص مضمونها تلاميذه: كابن خفيف، والطبري، وتلاميذ تلاميذه – وخصوصا ابن فورك والباقلاني – ومَنْ بعدهم كالجويني.
As for what some of his biographers say, that his teacher al-Jubba'i had a pen and ability for authorship, but did not have the same ability for discussion and debate in the heated gatherings at that time in Basra and Baghdad, and his young disciple Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari had eloquent speech and clarity but no involvement in authorship, so he would delegate him in his place when invited to these gatherings and confrontations – even if that is true regarding al-Jubba'i, it is not true regarding a man whose works reach a hundred or hundreds, which he gives us lists of during his lifetime, and which his students mentioned, explained some of them, and summarized their contents: like Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, and the students of his students – especially Ibn Furak and al-Baqillani – and those after them like al-Juwayni.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage addresses a claim made by some biographers of al-Ash'ari. The claim is that al-Ash'ari's teacher, al-Jubba'i, was skilled in writing and authorship but not in oral debate, whereas al-Ash'ari was eloquent in speech but not involved in authorship. Thus al-Jubba'i would send al-Ash'ari to debate in his place. The author of this introduction (the editor) responds: even if that claim were true for al-Jubba'i, it is not true for al-Ash'ari, because al-Ash'ari's works number in the hundreds. He himself provided lists of his works during his lifetime. His students — such as Ibn Khafif and al-Tabari — and later students like Ibn Furak and al-Baqillani, and even later figures like al-Juwayni, mentioned these works, explained some of them, and summarized their contents. The passage thus refutes the idea that al-Ash'ari was not an author, emphasizing his prolific written output.

Key Terms
الجبائي
أبو الحسن الأشعري
ابن فورك
الباقلاني
الجويني

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari was only an eloquent orator and did not write books.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari authored hundreds of works, as evidenced by his own lists and the testimony of his students and later scholars.

Checkpoint
What evidence does the passage use to refute the claim that al-Ash'ari was not involved in authorship?
A) His teacher al-Jubba'i said so.
B) His works number a hundred or hundreds, and lists were provided by him and his students.
C) He only wrote one book, al-Luma'.
D) He was not interested in writing.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's extensive written corpus disproves the notion that he was solely an oral debater.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever assumed someone's credibility based on one skill (like speaking) without considering their other contributions? How can you use al-Ash'ari's example to avoid such narrow judgments in your own life?
?
When you learn about a scholar, do you value their written works as much as their oral teachings? What concrete step can you take to engage more with primary texts rather than just listening to summaries?
?
The biographers' error shows how even early accounts can be incomplete. Are you willing to question popular narratives about scholars or even people you admire? How might this lesson change how you verify information before forming an opinion?

Al-Ash'ari's Objective Method in Maqalat al-Islamiyyin
Editor describes al-Ash'ari's objective method in Maqalat al-Islamiyyin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari adopted an objective methodology in presenting the views of different Islamic sects in his seminal work 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin'.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari presented every sect's beliefs as they saw themselves, not as their opponents wished to portray them.

In this opening passage, the editor highlights the distinctive approach of Imam al-Ash'ari in his famous book 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin'. Rather than polemicizing or distorting opposing views, al-Ash'ari undertook to present each group's doctrines with complete honesty and objectivity. This set a new standard for scholarly discourse in Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Read about al-Ash'ari's motivation
Notice that the editor says al-Ash'ari devoted himself to studying various intellectual currents and presented them as their own followers see them.
2
Identify the objective method
The passage emphasises that al-Ash'ari did not leave this task to others but undertook it himself in a wonderful manner, objectively, and then supplemented it with discussion and refutation in other works.
3
Connect to al-Luma'
The editor notes that al-Luma' is one of his works where he engaged in critical discussion alongside objective presentation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومقولات فكرية متنوعة باطنية، وظاهرية فلسفية ونصية، شيعية وسنية خارجية وجماعية، فانتدب نفسه لذلك، وتوفَّرَ على دراستها، وعرضها بكل أمانة كما يرى أهلها أنفسهم، لا كما يرغب خصومهم أن يصوّروها، حسبما يفيد كتابه الفذ : مقالات الإسلاميين واختلافات المصلين (١)، فلم يترك ذلك لغيره، بل نهض به على نحو رائع، في كتابه المذكور، موضوعيًا، ثم مصحوبًا بالمناقشة والرد والجواب والرفض في سائر مؤلفاته الأخرى، ومنها «اللمع» بوجه خاص (٢).
أما ما يقوله بعض من مؤرخيه من أن أستاذه الجبائي، كان ذا قلم وقدرة على التأليف، وليس له القدرة نفسها على المناقشة والجدل، في المجالس المحتدمة حينذاك، في البصرة وبغداد، وكان تلميذه الشاب «أبو الحسن الأشعري» ذا لسان وبيان ولا اشتغال له بالتأليف، فكان ينتدبه بدلا منه إذا دُعِيَ لهذه المجالس والمواجهات – فلئن صح ذلك بالنسبة للجبائي، فليس صحيحًا في حق رجل، تبلغ مؤلفاته المئةَ أو المئات، وهي التي يعطينا قوائم بها في حياته، والتي ذكرها، وشرح بعضها، ولخص مضمونها تلاميذه: كابن خفيف، والطبري، وتلاميذ تلاميذه – وخصوصا ابن فورك والباقلاني – ومَنْ بعدهم كالجويني. (١) وفي هذا العنوان اختلاف، ولكنه يعبر عن مضمون الكتاب، ويكشف عن هدف مؤلفه. انظر : ابن عساكر : تبيين كذب المفتري ١٣٠ وما بعدها.
(٢) انظر اللمع، تحقيق غرابة – المقدمة، ص ٦ .
والإسفراييني. وهي التي عارضها خصومه ونقضوها، أو البعض منها، ومن هذا البعض كتاب «اللمع». وتبلغ هذه المؤلفات المئة أو تزيد ومنها كتاب التفسير المفقود الآن، للأسف الشديد، وقد بلغ مئة أو مئتي ملزمة على الأقل، أي أنه بلغ قرابة ألفي صفحة؛ ككتاب تأويلات أهل السنة الذي كتبه في التفسير، نظيره فيما وراء النهر، أبو منصور الماتريدي (٣٣٣هـ)، ونُشِرَ أخيرًا، في إستانبول، في عشر مجلدات.
وقد تجاوز البحث العلمي ذلك كله كما قلنا آنفا - حينما نشر المستشرق الفرنسي دانيال جيماريه النص الناسخ لهذه الآراء والتأويلات؛ أعني كتاب ابن فُورَك : «مجرد مقالات أبي الحسن الأشعري» (١)، ومنذ أن عقد «الأزهر الشريف» مؤتمره العالمي، حول الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري ونشر أبحاث هذا المؤتمر في أربع مجلدات كبار - نقول : تجاوز البحث العلمي المعاصر مقولة : إن بناء المذهب المنسوب للأشعري، إنما يرجع إلى جهود تلاميذه المباشرين، أو غير المباشرين، وبخاصة أبو بكر الباقلاني (٢) (٤٠٣هـ)، وإن كنا نعذر القائلين بهذا الرأي (٢) بالعذر الواضح، وهو قلة المصادر حينذاك، أما وقد أُتيحت لنا - بحمد الله - مصادر (١) راجع ص ٦، ٧ من هذه المقدمة.
(٢) انظر مقدمة نشرة الدكتور حمودة للمع للباقلاني، ص٨ وما بعدها. ص ٥، ٦، ومقدمة التمهيد
And various intellectual currents: esoteric, exoteric, philosophical, textual, Shiite, Sunni, external, and communal, so he devoted himself to that, and studied them thoroughly, and presented them with complete honesty as their own adherents see them, not as their opponents wish to portray them, according to his unique book: 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin wa-Ikhtilaf al-Musallin' (1). So he did not leave that to others, but undertook it in a wonderful manner, in that mentioned book, objectively, then accompanied by discussion, refutation, response, and rejection in his other works, especially 'al-Luma' (2).
As for what some of his historians say, that his teacher al-Jubba'i had a pen and ability in authorship, but did not have the same ability in debate and argument in the heated sessions at that time in Basra and Baghdad, and that his young student Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari had eloquence and exposition and no involvement in authorship, so he would commission him in his place when invited to these sessions and confrontations – if that is correct regarding al-Jubba'i, it is not correct regarding a man whose works number one hundred or hundreds, which he gives us lists of in his lifetime, and which he mentioned, and some of which he explained, and whose content was summarized by his students: like Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, and the students of his students – especially Ibn Furak and al-Baqillani – and those after them like al-Juwayni. (1) There is disagreement about this title, but it expresses the content of the book and reveals the author's aim. See: Ibn 'Asakir: Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari 130 ff.
(2) See al-Luma', ed. Gharaba – Introduction, p. 6.
And al-Isfara'ini. And these works were opposed by his opponents and refuted, or some of them, and among this some is the book 'al-Luma'. And these works number one hundred or more, among them the book of tafsir now lost, unfortunately, which reached one hundred or two hundred parts at least, that is, it reached nearly two thousand pages; like the book 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna' which he wrote in tafsir, its counterpart in Transoxiana is Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (d. 333 AH), and it was recently published in Istanbul in ten volumes.
And scholarly research has gone beyond all that as we said earlier – when the French orientalist Daniel Gimaret published the copyist text of these views and interpretations; I mean the book of Ibn Furak: 'Mujarrad Maqalat al-Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' (1), and since al-Azhar al-Sharif held its international conference on Imam Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and published the research of this conference in four large volumes – we say: contemporary scholarly research has surpassed the statement that the construction of the school attributed to al-Ash'ari is due to the efforts of his direct or indirect students, especially Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (2) (d. 403 AH), although we excuse those who hold this opinion (2) with the clear excuse, which is the scarcity of sources at that time. But now that we have – praise be to God – sources (1) See pp. 6, 7 of this introduction.
(2) See the introduction of Dr. Hamuda's edition of al-Luma' for al-Baqillani, p. 8 ff.; and introduction of al-Tamhid, pp. 5, 6.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction by the editor. It begins by praising al-Ash'ari's objective method in his book 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin': he presented each sect's views as they themselves see them, not as opponents portray them. The editor then addresses a historical claim that al-Ash'ari's teacher al-Jubba'i was a writer but not a debater, so he would send his student al-Ash'ari to debates. The editor refutes this by noting that al-Ash'ari wrote hundreds of works himself, as evidenced by lists from his lifetime and summaries by his students (Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, etc.). He then notes the vast quantity of al-Ash'ari's lost and extant works, including a massive lost tafsir comparable to al-Maturidi's. Finally, the editor discusses modern scholarship: the publication of Gimaret's edition of Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad' and the Azhar conference have overturned the earlier view that the Ash'ari school was built mainly by later disciples like al-Baqillani. The editor excuses earlier scholars due to lack of sources but asserts that now, with abundant sources, this view is surpassed.

Key Terms
مقالات الإسلاميين
اللمع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how did al-Ash'ari present the views of different sects in 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin'?
A) As his own beliefs
B) As their opponents saw them
C) As their own adherents saw them
D) He did not present them at all

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's first step was to objectively present each sect's own self-understanding before offering any critique.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a person or group you strongly disagree with, do you first try to understand their beliefs from their own perspective, or do you rely on what their opponents say? What would change if you adopted al-Ash'ari's method of honest presentation before critique?
?
Al-Ash'ari devoted himself to studying every sect, including those he would later refute. What is one viewpoint you avoid examining because it challenges your comfort or assumptions? What concrete step will you take this week to understand it from its adherents' perspective?
?
If you were to write a 'Maqalat' of your own about those you differ with, would you be able to present their views 'as they see themselves' without distortion? What does your answer reveal about your own intellectual honesty?

Life of Imam al-Ashari

Refuting the Legend: Al-Ash'ari as Author, Not Just Debater
Editor refutes the legend that al-Ash'ari only debated for his teacher and had no works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the editor refutes the claim that al-Ash'ari merely debated for his teacher al-Jubba'i, and the evidence for al-Ash'ari's extensive authorship.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari authored hundreds of works; he was not merely a stand-in debater for his teacher.

A common story about al-Ash'ari claims that his teacher al-Jubba'i would send him to debates because al-Ash'ari was eloquent but had no involvement in writing. In this passage, the editor confronts this legend head-on, pointing to the overwhelming evidence of al-Ash'ari's own prolific authorship, as attested by lists from his lifetime and the summaries of his students.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical claim
The editor reports what some historians say: al-Jubba'i was a writer but not a debater, so he sent al-Ash'ari to debates.
2
Identify the refutation
The editor says that even if this were true for al-Jubba'i, it is not true for a man whose works number in the hundreds.
3
Notice the evidence
The editor lists evidence: lists of works from al-Ash'ari's lifetime, his own explanations, and summaries by his students like Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, and al-Juwayni.
4
Reflect on the implication
Thus, the legend is false; al-Ash'ari was a prolific author, not just a debater.

Modern Scholarship and the Ash'ari School's Formation
Editor discusses how modern scholarship has superseded the view that later disciples built the Ash'ari school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how contemporary research has overturned the view that the Ash'ari school was built mainly by later disciples like al-Baqillani.

Core Idea
Modern publications show al-Ash'ari's own works were foundational; the school was not created solely by later disciples.

For a long time, some scholars thought that the Ash'ari school was largely the product of later theologians like al-Baqillani, due to limited access to al-Ash'ari's original works. But the editor notes that with the publication of key texts like Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad' and the Azhar conference, contemporary research has surpassed this view, while still excusing earlier scholars for their limited sources.

Guided Path
1
Read the scholarly context
The editor refers to the publication of Gimaret's edition of Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad Maqalat Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' and the Azhar conference on al-Ash'ari.
2
Identify the old view
The old view was that the Ash'ari school's construction was due to his students, especially al-Baqillani.
3
Understand the correction
Now with abundant sources, we see that al-Ash'ari himself laid the foundation; earlier scholars are excused due to scarcity of sources.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومقولات فكرية متنوعة باطنية، وظاهرية فلسفية ونصية، شيعية وسنية خارجية وجماعية، فانتدب نفسه لذلك، وتوفَّرَ على دراستها، وعرضها بكل أمانة كما يرى أهلها أنفسهم، لا كما يرغب خصومهم أن يصوّروها، حسبما يفيد كتابه الفذ : مقالات الإسلاميين واختلافات المصلين (١)، فلم يترك ذلك لغيره، بل نهض به على نحو رائع، في كتابه المذكور، موضوعيًا، ثم مصحوبًا بالمناقشة والرد والجواب والرفض في سائر مؤلفاته الأخرى، ومنها «اللمع» بوجه خاص (٢).
أما ما يقوله بعض من مؤرخيه من أن أستاذه الجبائي، كان ذا قلم وقدرة على التأليف، وليس له القدرة نفسها على المناقشة والجدل، في المجالس المحتدمة حينذاك، في البصرة وبغداد، وكان تلميذه الشاب «أبو الحسن الأشعري» ذا لسان وبيان ولا اشتغال له بالتأليف، فكان ينتدبه بدلا منه إذا دُعِيَ لهذه المجالس والمواجهات – فلئن صح ذلك بالنسبة للجبائي، فليس صحيحًا في حق رجل، تبلغ مؤلفاته المئةَ أو المئات، وهي التي يعطينا قوائم بها في حياته، والتي ذكرها، وشرح بعضها، ولخص مضمونها تلاميذه: كابن خفيف، والطبري، وتلاميذ تلاميذه – وخصوصا ابن فورك والباقلاني – ومَنْ بعدهم كالجويني. (١) وفي هذا العنوان اختلاف، ولكنه يعبر عن مضمون الكتاب، ويكشف عن هدف مؤلفه. انظر : ابن عساكر : تبيين كذب المفتري ١٣٠ وما بعدها.
(٢) انظر اللمع، تحقيق غرابة – المقدمة، ص ٦ .
والإسفراييني. وهي التي عارضها خصومه ونقضوها، أو البعض منها، ومن هذا البعض كتاب «اللمع». وتبلغ هذه المؤلفات المئة أو تزيد ومنها كتاب التفسير المفقود الآن، للأسف الشديد، وقد بلغ مئة أو مئتي ملزمة على الأقل، أي أنه بلغ قرابة ألفي صفحة؛ ككتاب تأويلات أهل السنة الذي كتبه في التفسير، نظيره فيما وراء النهر، أبو منصور الماتريدي (٣٣٣هـ)، ونُشِرَ أخيرًا، في إستانبول، في عشر مجلدات.
وقد تجاوز البحث العلمي ذلك كله كما قلنا آنفا - حينما نشر المستشرق الفرنسي دانيال جيماريه النص الناسخ لهذه الآراء والتأويلات؛ أعني كتاب ابن فُورَك : «مجرد مقالات أبي الحسن الأشعري» (١)، ومنذ أن عقد «الأزهر الشريف» مؤتمره العالمي، حول الإمام أبي الحسن الأشعري ونشر أبحاث هذا المؤتمر في أربع مجلدات كبار - نقول : تجاوز البحث العلمي المعاصر مقولة : إن بناء المذهب المنسوب للأشعري، إنما يرجع إلى جهود تلاميذه المباشرين، أو غير المباشرين، وبخاصة أبو بكر الباقلاني (٢) (٤٠٣هـ)، وإن كنا نعذر القائلين بهذا الرأي (٢) بالعذر الواضح، وهو قلة المصادر حينذاك، أما وقد أُتيحت لنا - بحمد الله - مصادر (١) راجع ص ٦، ٧ من هذه المقدمة.
(٢) انظر مقدمة نشرة الدكتور حمودة للمع للباقلاني، ص٨ وما بعدها. ص ٥، ٦، ومقدمة التمهيد
And various intellectual currents: esoteric, exoteric, philosophical, textual, Shiite, Sunni, external, and communal, so he devoted himself to that, and studied them thoroughly, and presented them with complete honesty as their own adherents see them, not as their opponents wish to portray them, according to his unique book: 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin wa-Ikhtilaf al-Musallin' (1). So he did not leave that to others, but undertook it in a wonderful manner, in that mentioned book, objectively, then accompanied by discussion, refutation, response, and rejection in his other works, especially 'al-Luma' (2).
As for what some of his historians say, that his teacher al-Jubba'i had a pen and ability in authorship, but did not have the same ability in debate and argument in the heated sessions at that time in Basra and Baghdad, and that his young student Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari had eloquence and exposition and no involvement in authorship, so he would commission him in his place when invited to these sessions and confrontations – if that is correct regarding al-Jubba'i, it is not correct regarding a man whose works number one hundred or hundreds, which he gives us lists of in his lifetime, and which he mentioned, and some of which he explained, and whose content was summarized by his students: like Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, and the students of his students – especially Ibn Furak and al-Baqillani – and those after them like al-Juwayni. (1) There is disagreement about this title, but it expresses the content of the book and reveals the author's aim. See: Ibn 'Asakir: Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari 130 ff.
(2) See al-Luma', ed. Gharaba – Introduction, p. 6.
And al-Isfara'ini. And these works were opposed by his opponents and refuted, or some of them, and among this some is the book 'al-Luma'. And these works number one hundred or more, among them the book of tafsir now lost, unfortunately, which reached one hundred or two hundred parts at least, that is, it reached nearly two thousand pages; like the book 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna' which he wrote in tafsir, its counterpart in Transoxiana is Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (d. 333 AH), and it was recently published in Istanbul in ten volumes.
And scholarly research has gone beyond all that as we said earlier – when the French orientalist Daniel Gimaret published the copyist text of these views and interpretations; I mean the book of Ibn Furak: 'Mujarrad Maqalat al-Shaykh Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari' (1), and since al-Azhar al-Sharif held its international conference on Imam Abi al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and published the research of this conference in four large volumes – we say: contemporary scholarly research has surpassed the statement that the construction of the school attributed to al-Ash'ari is due to the efforts of his direct or indirect students, especially Abu Bakr al-Baqillani (2) (d. 403 AH), although we excuse those who hold this opinion (2) with the clear excuse, which is the scarcity of sources at that time. But now that we have – praise be to God – sources (1) See pp. 6, 7 of this introduction.
(2) See the introduction of Dr. Hamuda's edition of al-Luma' for al-Baqillani, p. 8 ff.; and introduction of al-Tamhid, pp. 5, 6.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction by the editor. It begins by praising al-Ash'ari's objective method in his book 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin': he presented each sect's views as they themselves see them, not as opponents portray them. The editor then addresses a historical claim that al-Ash'ari's teacher al-Jubba'i was a writer but not a debater, so he would send his student al-Ash'ari to debates. The editor refutes this by noting that al-Ash'ari wrote hundreds of works himself, as evidenced by lists from his lifetime and summaries by his students (Ibn Khafif, al-Tabari, Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, etc.). He then notes the vast quantity of al-Ash'ari's lost and extant works, including a massive lost tafsir comparable to al-Maturidi's. Finally, the editor discusses modern scholarship: the publication of Gimaret's edition of Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad' and the Azhar conference have overturned the earlier view that the Ash'ari school was built mainly by later disciples like al-Baqillani. The editor excuses earlier scholars due to lack of sources but asserts that now, with abundant sources, this view is surpassed.

Key Terms
مجرّد مقالات أبي الحسن الأشعري
الباقلاني
الأزهر
جيماريه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Ash'ari school was entirely constructed by al-Baqillani and later disciples, not by al-Ash'ari himself.
Correction: Modern scholarship shows that al-Ash'ari's own works, now available, were foundational; the school was not solely the product of later disciples.

Checkpoint
What development does the editor cite as allowing contemporary research to surpass the view that the Ash'ari school was built by later disciples?
A) The discovery of al-Ash'ari's tomb
B) Publication of Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad' and the Azhar conference
C) The translation of al-Ash'ari's works into French
D) The opening of a new library in Basra

Key Takeaway
With modern publications, we now recognize that al-Ash'ari's own works were the foundation of the school attributed to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that earlier scholars were excused for lacking primary sources. You have no such excuse with modern publications. Are you actively reading the foundational works of Islamic theology, or are you relying on secondhand accounts? What concrete step will you take this week to access a primary source?
?
The shift in scholarly opinion shows how easily we accept narratives without checking original evidence. In your own life, where have you accepted a claim about your faith without verifying it from the Quran and Sunnah? Will you commit to investigating one such claim this month?
?
The editor notes that modern sources have changed understanding. If you were to die today, would your knowledge of Islamic theology be based on superficial hearsay or deep, firsthand study? What will you do to ensure you are not among those who 'excuse' themselves due to lack of effort?

Al-Ash'ari's Many Works and Lost Tafsir
Editorial note on al-Ash'ari's extensive works and lost tafsir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extensive literary output of Imam al-Ash'ari, including details of his lost tafsir that rivaled al-Maturidi's work in scope.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari wrote over 100 works, including a massive tafsir now lost.

This lesson presents an editorial note highlighting the immense scholarly legacy of Imam al-Ash'ari. It focuses on the sheer volume of his writings—over one hundred works—and the unfortunate loss of his monumental Qur'an commentary, which was comparable in size to al-Maturidi's ten-volume tafsir.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic source and its translation. Notice that it mentions 'Al-Luma' as one work among many, and then describes the lost tafsir.
This is an editorial note, not a theological argument.
2
Identify the scale of al-Ash'ari's output
The passage states that his writings number one hundred or more. Let this sink in: he was extraordinarily prolific.
Contrast this with common perceptions of a single work.
3
Reflect on the lost tafsir
Consider the size: one to two hundred fascicles, approximately two thousand pages. Compare this to contemporary published tafasir to appreciate the loss.
The comparison to al-Maturidi's work illustrates the scale.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللُّمَع في الردّ على أَهلِ الزَّيْغِ والبدع والإسفراييني. وهي التي عارضها خصومه ونقضوها، أو البعض منها، ومن هذا البعض كتاب «اللمع». وتبلغ هذه المؤلفات المئة أو تزيد ومنها كتاب التفسير المفقود الآن، للأسف الشديد، وقد بلغ مئة أو مئتي ملزمة على الأقل، أي أنه بلغ قرابة ألفي صفحة؛ ككتاب تأويلات أهل السنة الذي كتبه في التفسير، نظيره فيما وراء النهر، أبو منصور الماتريدي (٣٣٣هـ)، ونُشِرَ أخيرًا، في إستانبول، في عشر مجلدات.
'Al-Luma' in refutation of the people of deviation and innovation and al-Isfarayini. And they are the ones which his opponents opposed and refuted, or some of them, and from this some is the book 'Al-Luma'. And these writings reach one hundred or more, and among them is the book of tafsir now lost, unfortunately, and it reached one hundred or two hundred fascicles at least, meaning it reached nearly two thousand pages; like the book 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna' which he wrote in tafsir, its counterpart beyond the river, Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (333 AH), and it was recently published in Istanbul in ten volumes.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note discussing the extensive body of works authored by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins by mentioning the book 'Al-Luma' itself as part of a larger corpus. The editor then states that al-Ash'ari's writings number one hundred or more, among which is a massive tafsir (Qur'an commentary) that is now lost. This tafsir was extremely large, consisting of one to two hundred fascicles, roughly two thousand pages—comparable in scale to the tafsir 'Ta'wilat Ahl al-Sunna' by al-Maturidi, which has been recently published in ten volumes. The purpose of this note is to emphasize the scholarly productivity of al-Ash'ari and to highlight the loss of a major work.

Predecessors and Posthumous Naming
Editorial acknowledgment that al-Ash'ari was preceded by earlier theologians who influenced him

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Ash'ari was not the first to use kalam for Ahl al-Sunna, but that he synthesized earlier efforts and his school was recognized posthumously.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari built on earlier theologians, but his synthesis became the dominant school.

This passage acknowledges that al-Ash'ari had predecessors who engaged in theological reasoning for Ahl al-Sunna. He frequently quoted them, and his own school was named only after his death. Yet this does not diminish his unique role; rather, it shows how his work crystallized earlier traditions. The editor affirms that the school's naming after him reflects his posthumous influence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the list of names and the flow of the editor's argument.
The passage is one continuous paragraph.
2
Identify the predecessors
Look for the names of earlier scholars listed. What was their contribution? The text says they preceded al-Ash'ari in building the school theologically.
Ibn Kullab, al-Muhasibi, al-Qalanisi, al-Junayd, al-Salihi, and others.
3
Understand the editor's point about Ibn Taymiyya
The passage mentions Ibn Taymiyya's discussion of 'al-Kullabiyya' and its influence. Why is this brought up? To show that the intellectual lineage is known and debated.
The editor says this is natural and does not diminish al-Ash'ari's role.
4
Reflect on the naming of the school
Notice when the school was named after al-Ash'ari: after his death. What does this signify? It shows that the school's recognition came posthumously, based on widespread acceptance.
The majority of Muslims now follow him.
5
Answer the checkpoint question
Test your understanding by answering the question about which scholar al-Ash'ari accepted the definition of faith from.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعم، إن الرجل مسبوق في محاولته بناء مذهب أهل السنة والجماعة كلاميًا؛ أي من خلال منهج يجمع العقل والنقل، ويواجه الشبه التي يروجها المخالفون بالرَّدِّ والنقض، والدفاع عن الموقف، وهو نفسه كثيرًا ما ينقل عن بعض أصحابنا، وافقهم أو خالفهم؛ وفي مقدمتهم: ابنُ كلاب (٢٤٠هـ، وقيل: ٢٤١هـ)، والمحاسبي (٢٤٣هـ)، والقَلانِيُّ ( كان معاصرًا للشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري)، والجنيد (۲۹۸هـ)، والصالحيُّ الذي يرتضي قوله في مسألة تعريف الإيمان (۲)، وغيرهم. وحديث ابن تيمية وأصحابه «الكلَّابية وأثرها في الأشعري والأشعرية، معلوم ومشتهر (۳)، ولكن ذلك أمر طبيعي في الحياة الفكرية وهو لا ينقص من قيمة الدور الذي نهض به أبو الحسن، ولم تكن تسمية المذهب باسمه بعد رحيله إلى جوار ربه عز وجل - ومتابعة أكثر المسلمين في العالم عنه (١)
Yes, the man was preceded in his attempt to build the school of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a theologically; that is, through a methodology that combines reason and transmission, and confronts the doubts spread by opponents with refutation and rebuttal, and defense of the position. And he himself frequently transmits from some of our companions, whether he agreed with them or disagreed; and foremost among them: Ibn Kullab (240 AH, and it is said 241 AH), al-Muhasibi (243 AH), al-Qalanisi (who was contemporary with Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari), al-Junayd (298 AH), and al-Salihi whose statement he accepted in the issue of defining faith (2), and others. And the discussion of Ibn Taymiyya and his followers regarding 'al-Kullabiyya and its influence on al-Ash'ari and the Ash'aris' is known and famous (3). But that is a natural thing in intellectual life and it does not diminish the value of the role undertaken by Abu al-Hasan. And the naming of the school after him occurred after his departure to his Lord, may He be glorified and exalted - and the majority of Muslims in the world follow him.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is an editorial clarification that al-Ash'ari was not the first to engage in kalam (theological argumentation) for Ahl al-Sunna. He was preceded by scholars like Ibn Kullab, al-Muhasibi, al-Qalanisi, al-Junayd, and al-Salihi. The editor notes that al-Ash'ari often quotes these earlier figures. The passage also references the well-known discussion by Ibn Taymiyya about the 'Kullabiyya' school and its influence on al-Ash'ari. However, the editor argues that this intellectual indebtedness is natural and does not diminish al-Ash'ari's own contributions. Finally, it points out that the school was named after him only after his death, and that the majority of Muslims now follow his school. This underscores the posthumous recognition and widespread acceptance.

الكلابية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Al-Ash'ari had no predecessors and created the school from scratch.
Correction: Al-Ash'ari was preceded by scholars like Ibn Kullab, al-Muhasibi, etc., and his school was named after him only after his death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If al-Ash'ari built on the work of others and the school was named later, what does that tell you about your own responsibility to both learn from predecessors and contribute to the tradition? What are you actively passing on?

Ash'ari's Students and the Development of His School
Editor describes Ash'ari's students and their role in clarifying the school.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Ash'ari's students and later scholars transmitted and developed his theological school, and why his foundational role remains central.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's school was built by his students, but his own works remain the foundation.

This passage from the editor of al-Luma' provides a historical overview of how Imam al-Ash'ari's school (madhhab) was transmitted and developed by his direct and indirect students. It names key figures and highlights their role in clarifying and defending the school, while affirming that the foundational contribution remains Ash'ari's own.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first direct students, then indirect, then their collective role, then Ash'ari's unique foundational role.
The passage is a single paragraph with a clear logical flow.
2
Identify the two categories of students
Find the two groups: direct students (unnamed but described as 'intellectual luminaries') and indirect students (named: al-Baqillani, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, Ibn Furak, and later figures).
The editor notes that one researcher has studied the direct students.
3
Understand the role of the later scholars
The later Ash'ari scholars are said to have clarified, refined, explained, and defended the school against opponents and distorters.
4
Recognize Ash'ari's foundational role
Despite the contributions of many, the editor insists that the foundational role belongs to Ash'ari alone, listing his major works and asserting consistency among them.
This counters any claim of contradiction within Ash'ari's writings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نعم، لقد كان تلاميذه الكُثر كما ذكرنا في موطن آخر - أعلاما مفكرين، وقد تناولهم بالعناية أحد أصحابنا الباحثين، أما تلاميذه غير المباشرين فيكفي إيراد أسمائهم: كالباقلاني، وأبي إسحاق الإسفراييني وابن فورك، وكلهم، ومَنْ جاء بعدهم، من أمثال إمام الحرمين الجويني، والغزالي، والرازي، والآمدي وعلماء العصور التالية من الأشاعرة كان لهم جميعًا دورهم الذي لا ينكر في إيضاح المذهب وتنقيحه، وشرحه وتوضيحه، والرد على مخالفيه من أهل الزيغ والبدع، أو شأن محرفيه والمفترين عليه وعلى رجاله في كل وقت وحين، المذاهب الكلامية جميعًا. ولكن يبقى الدور التأسيسي حقًا خالصًا، وتاجًا مطمئنا على جبين صاحب «اللمع»، و«المقالات»، و«الاستحسان»، و«الحث»، و«المختزن»، و«الإبانة» الذي لا يتناقض أبدًا - كما لاحظ شيخنا غرابة – مع «اللمع» أو المؤلفات الأخرى للأشعري.
Yes, his many students, as we mentioned elsewhere, were intellectual luminaries, and one of our fellow researchers took care of them. As for his indirect students, it suffices to mention their names: al-Baqillani, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, Ibn Furak, all of them, and those who came after them, such as Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, al-Ghazali, al-Razi, al-Amidi, and the scholars of the later Ash'ari ages – all of them had their undeniable role in clarifying the school, refining it, explaining and elucidating it, refuting its opponents from the people of deviation and innovation, and countering those who distort it and slander it and its men at all times, among all theological schools. But the foundational role remains truly pure, a secure crown upon the brow of the author of 'al-Luma', 'al-Maqalat', 'al-Istihsan', 'al-Hathth', 'al-Mukhtazan', and 'al-Ibana', which never contradicts – as our teacher Ghuraba observed – with 'al-Luma' or the other works of al-Ash'ari.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and historical commentary on the transmission of Ash'ari's school. The editor first affirms that Ash'ari's many direct students were intellectual luminaries, and notes that one of their own researchers has studied them. Then he lists prominent indirect students: al-Baqillani, Abu Ishaq al-Isfarayini, Ibn Furak, and later figures like al-Juwayni, al-Ghazali, al-Razi, and al-Amidi. He states that all of them had an undeniable role in clarifying, refining, explaining, and defending the school against opponents and distorters. However, he emphasizes that the foundational role remains uniquely and purely that of Ash'ari himself, as author of several key works, and asserts that there is no contradiction between these works, contrary to some claims.

أعلام
مذهب
تمذهب

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ash'ari's influence was solely due to his lineage or position.
Correction: This passage shows that his school was transmitted and developed through his students and methodology, but his own writings remain foundational.

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's school was developed through a chain of scholars, but his own works remain the authoritative foundation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Immense Output of Imam al-Ash'ari
Describes the vast number of Ash'ari's works and his grand tafsir al-Mukhtazan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extraordinary scale of Imam al-Ash'ari's scholarly production as described by Ibn Hazm.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari authored hundreds of works, including a tafsir of nearly 500 volumes.

Imam al-Ash'ari is known not only for his theological legacy but also for his immense literary output. This passage from a biographical source gives us a vivid picture of his productivity, with his works numbering in the hundreds and his tafsir alone spanning an astonishing number of volumes. Let's dive into the details.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without overthinking. Then read the English translation to grasp the overall meaning.
Notice the key numbers mentioned: over 100 books, some say 300, and the tafsir has nearly 500 volumes.
2
Identify the key numbers and terms
Focus on the numbers: how many books did he write? How many volumes was his tafsir? Also note the terms 'juz'' and 'mulzamah'.
The term 'mulzamah' is compared to a modern bundle of pages.
3
Understand the size comparison
Ibn Hazm says a 'juz'' in their time is like a 'mulzamah', which the author estimates as about 8,000 pages in modern terms. Think about how massive that is.
This helps us appreciate the scale of al-Ash'ari's work.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: What does this enormous output tell us about Imam al-Ash'ari's dedication and influence? How does it support his role as a founding figure of Ash'ari theology?
This lesson is a window into his scholarly legacy.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مؤلفاته :
تبين الفقرات السابقة أنَّ شيخنا أبا الحسن كان مؤلفًا محترفًا، زادت مؤلفاته على مِئَةٍ كتاب، بل بلغ بعضهم بها الثلاثمئة ، ومنها - وهو تفسيره الكبير المسمى بالمختزن- ما يبلغ نحو خمسمئة جزء، كما قال ابن حزم والجزء عندهم قريب من «الملزمة» في العرف المعاصر، فيكون قرابة ثمانية آلاف صفحة في العُرفِ المعتاد الآن، على وجه التقريب حسب وصف ابن حزم - رحمه الله .
His works: The previous paragraphs show that our Shaykh Abu al-Hasan was a professional author; his works exceeded one hundred books, and some [authorities] reckoned them at three hundred. Among them is his great tafsir called al-Mukhtazan, which reaches nearly five hundred volumes, as Ibn Hazm said. A volume according to them is close to a 'mulzamah' in contemporary usage, so it would be about eight thousand pages in the usual custom now, approximately according to the description of Ibn Hazm - may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note on the prolific output of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari. It begins by stating that he was a professional author, with his works numbering over one hundred, and some authorities reporting up to three hundred. It highlights his great commentary on the Qur'an, titled al-Mukhtazan, which was enormous: nearly five hundred volumes. The passage then clarifies the size of a 'volume' (juz') in their terminology, comparing it to a contemporary 'mulzamah' (a term for a bundle of pages), and estimates the total page count at about eight thousand pages. The source for this information is Ibn Hazm.

ابن حزم
الجزء
الملزمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Imam al-Ash'ari wrote only a few books, perhaps a dozen or so.
Correction: This passage shows his works exceeded one hundred, with some authorities counting three hundred. His tafsir alone was nearly five hundred volumes.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari's scholarly output was immense, with works numbering in the hundreds and his tafsir al-Mukhtazan alone comprising nearly 500 volumes.

?
Ibn Hazm took the time to record the size of al-Mukhtazan for future generations. How will your deeds be recorded? Are you investing in what truly lasts for the Hereafter, or are you distracted by fleeting pursuits?

Historical Destruction of Ash‘ari’s Legacy
Lists causes for the loss of Ash‘ari’s works and contrasts with al-Maturidi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main causes for the loss of most of Imam al-Ash‘ari’s works: the Mongol invasion and deliberate destruction by opponents.

Core Idea
Most of Ash‘ari’s works were lost due to disasters and enemies.

Imam al-Ash‘ari authored many books, but few survive today. This lesson explores why: the Mongol sack of Baghdad and the hostility of the Mu‘tazili vizier Ibn ‘Abbad. Understanding this loss helps us appreciate the surviving texts.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage about destruction
Read the Arabic passage describing the Mongol invasion and Ibn ‘Abbad’s burning of books. Notice the vivid imagery of the Tigris turning black.
This sets the stage for understanding the scarcity.
2
Compare with al-Maturidi
The passage contrasts Ash‘ari’s fate with al-Maturidi, whose works survived better. Reflect on why this difference matters for later scholarship.
Al-Maturidi did not face the same local or foreign enemies.
3
Identify the consequences
Note the result: extreme scarcity and complaints from scholars and even Ash‘ari’s own students. This explains why his works are rare today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولئن كان معظم هذا التراث قد تبدد أو أُبيد، نتيجة الكوارث التاريخية كما فعلت جحافل المغول عند اقتحام بغداد، وتبديد تراثها الحضاري عام ٦٥٦هـ ، حتى اسودَّتْ مياه دجلة - كما رُوي ، أو بمسعى مُتَعَمَّدٍ مُنظم ، من خصومه الفكريين ، كما نُسب إلى الوزير ابن عبّادٍ، وزير الديالمة صاحب الاتجاه الاعتزالي؛ من يحرق، ويشجع على إتلاف الكتب التي أودعها الشيخ أبو الحسن ثمار فكره، وحصاد عمره وأحوال عصره، فحُرِمَ الناسُ من خيرٍ كثير - فأيا ما كان السبب في هذه الكارثة، فقد نجم عنها ندرة الكتب الباقية من تراثه في مكتبات وخزائن المخطوطات، في الشرق والغرب، واختفاء الأكثرية الساحقة ، منها ، أو ضياعها، وهو موضع شكوى الدارسين والباحثين المعاصرين، بل إن الجيل الثاني من تلاميذه يردِّدُون الشكوى نفسها (۱) . ولو قارنا المصير الذي لقيته مؤلفات الأشعري، ومؤلفات نظيره ومُعاصره الماتريدي، لظهر لنا الفرقُ الواضح بين الحالتين؛ لأن الأخير لحسن الحظ - لم يتعرض لمثل ما تعرض له الأشعري وتراثه الفكري من الخصوم المحليين أو الطغاة المهاجمين . ١- والفضلُ في معرفة حجم هذا التراث، وأسماء المؤلفات المفقودة أو المختفية حتى الآن يرجع إلى المؤلف نفسه -رحمه الله - الذي دون قائمة مؤلفاته التي أنجزها قبل سنة ٣٢٠هـ -وكان عندئذ في الستين من عمره - وذلك في كتابه «العُمَد في الرؤية»، وكذا إحالاته في بعضها على ما يرتبط بالموضوع نفسه في مؤلفات أخرى مما ورد إلينا بحمد الله ؛ فهو قد ذكر لنا بنفسه، في القائمة المشار إليها، التي أوردها في كتابه المذكور: أنه ربما أصدر الكتاب الواحد عدة إصدارات بأحجام متفاوتة، بحسب مقاصده منها، ومن ذلك كتاب «اللمع»، الذي نقدِّم بهذه اللمحات طبعة جديدة محققةً للنص الباقي منه في مخطوطة وحيدة، في العالم كله .
= وانظر الرواية التي أوردها الشيخ الكوثري بشأن موقف الصاحب ابن عباد من تفسير أبي الحسن الأشعري، في هامش ص ١٢٧ من كتاب تبيين كذب المفتري.
۱۲۷
Even if most of this heritage was scattered or destroyed as a result of historical disasters — as the Mongol hordes did when they stormed Baghdad and annihilated its civilizational heritage in the year 656 AH, until the waters of the Tigris turned black, as is narrated — or by a deliberate, organized effort from his intellectual opponents, as attributed to the vizier Ibn 'Abbad, the vizier of the Daylamites of Mu'tazili orientation, who burned and encouraged the destruction of the books in which Shaykh Abu al-Hasan deposited the fruits of his thought, the harvest of his life, and the circumstances of his era, so that people were deprived of much good. Whatever the cause of this calamity, it resulted in the scarcity of the remaining books from his heritage in libraries and manuscript repositories, in the East and West, and the disappearance of the vast majority of them, or their loss — a matter complained of by contemporary researchers and scholars. Indeed, the second generation of his disciples repeated the same complaint (1). And if we compare the fate that befell Ash'ari's works and those of his counterpart and contemporary al-Maturidi, the clear difference between the two situations would appear, because the latter, fortunately, did not experience what Ash'ari and his intellectual heritage experienced from local opponents or invading tyrants. The credit for knowing the size of this heritage and the names of the lost or hidden works up to now goes to the author himself — may Allah have mercy on him — who recorded a list of his works completed before the year 320 AH, when he was in his sixties, in his book 'al-'Umad fi al-Ru'ya', as well as his cross-references in some of them to what is related to the same topic in other works that have reached us, praise be to Allah. He mentioned to us himself, in the aforementioned list which he included in his mentioned book, that he might issue a single book in several editions of varying sizes according to his purposes from them, and among that is the book 'al-Luma', of which we present here with these glimpses a new critical edition of the remaining text from a unique manuscript in the entire world.
= And see the narration that al-Shaykh al-Kawthari mentioned regarding the stance of al-Sahib Ibn 'Abbad toward the tafsir of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, in the margin of p. 127 of the book 'Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari'.
127
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a historical account of the fate of Imam al-Ash'ari's written works. It begins by describing the causes of the loss: either natural disasters like the Mongol invasion of Baghdad in 656 AH, which destroyed countless manuscripts, or deliberate destruction by his opponents, especially the Mu'tazili vizier Ibn 'Abbad, who allegedly burned his books. The result was a severe scarcity of his works, lamented even by his own students. The passage then compares Ash'ari's fate with that of al-Maturidi, whose works survived better. It then explains that the main source for knowing the extent of Ash'ari's lost works is his own list written in his book 'al-'Umad fi al-Ru'ya', where he recorded his works before age sixty. It also notes that he sometimes issued multiple editions of the same book. Finally, it relates that the present edition of al-Luma' is based on the unique surviving manuscript. The passage ends with a reference to a narration by al-Kawthari.

Key Terms
المغول
ابن عباد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what two events led to the destruction of Ash‘ari’s works?
A) Mongol invasion and Ibn ‘Abbad’s burning
B) Only the Mongol invasion
C) Only Ibn ‘Abbad’s burning
D) Al-Maturidi’s suppression

Key Takeaway
The scarcity of Ash‘ari’s works is due to the Mongol sack of Baghdad and the targeted destruction by his intellectual opponents.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The passage shows that Ash'ari's works were destroyed by both external invaders and internal opponents. Which of these two threats to Islamic knowledge is more alive in your own community today, and what concrete step can you take to resist it?
?
Ibn 'Abbad burned books because he disagreed with their content. When you encounter a theological view you strongly oppose, do you ever 'burn' it by dismissing or ridiculing it without fair examination? What would it cost you to instead preserve and understand it first?
?
Al-Maturidi's works survived because his circumstances were spared from disaster. If your own knowledge and efforts were to be lost tomorrow, what would be left behind? Are you actively ensuring that the truth you hold is transmitted reliably to others?

Ash‘ari’s Own Catalogue and the Survival of al-Luma‘
Explains the source for knowing Ash‘ari’s lost works and the unique manuscript of al-Luma‘.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash‘ari himself recorded his works in ‘al-‘Umad fi al-Ru’ya’ and that only a unique manuscript of ‘al-Luma‘’ survives.

Core Idea
Ash‘ari preserved his own bibliography; al-Luma‘ exists in a single manuscript.

Despite the loss of most of his works, we know their names because Ash‘ari listed them. This lesson examines his self-cataloguing and the survival of his famous text ‘al-Luma‘’ in a unique manuscript.

Guided Path
1
Read about Ash‘ari’s list
Read the passage describing how Ash‘ari recorded a list of his works in ‘al-‘Umad fi al-Ru’ya’. Note that he was around sixty years old at the time.
This list is the primary source for knowing his lost works.
2
Understand multiple editions
The passage mentions that Ash‘ari sometimes issued multiple editions of the same book. This shows his intellectual productivity.
3
Learn about the unique manuscript of al-Luma‘
The passage ends by stating that the present edition of ‘al-Luma‘’ is based on the only surviving manuscript in the world. Reflect on the rarity of such texts.
The footnote provides additional information about Ibn ‘Abbad’s attitude.

Ibn Furak: Preserver of Ash'ari's Legacy
Compares Ibn Furak to earlier preservers of madhhab works and mentions Gimaret's publication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the crucial role of Ibn Furak in preserving and transmitting the teachings of Imam al-Ash'ari, and how his work compares to earlier preservers of other madhhabs.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak was the 'Muhammad al-Shaybani' of the Ash'ari school, a second-generation transmitter of orthodoxy.

This lesson highlights the pivotal figure of Ibn Furak, who dedicated himself to recording and transmitting the views of Imam al-Ash'ari. While not a direct student, his systematic compilation ensured that Ash'ari's legacy survived. The passage compares his work to earlier preservers of other schools and notes a modern edition of his key book.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify Ibn Furak's role
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that the author compares Ibn Furak to specific earlier scholars.
He is called 'al-Ustadh' and described as a peer of al-Baqillani.
2
Understand the comparison with earlier preservers
The author likens Ibn Furak to Muhammad al-Shaybani for Abu Hanifa, and to Sahnun and Ibn Abi Zayd for Malik. Think about what these figures did: they collected and systematized the teachings of their imams.
3
Consider the modern dimension
Gimaret published Ibn Furak's 'Mujarrad Maqalat'. Note the mixed reception: praised but also criticized by some Arab researchers.
4
Reflect on the significance of indirect transmission
Ibn Furak was a second-generation student. This shows that preserving a school's teachings often requires dedicated scholars from later generations.
This addresses a common misunderstanding that only direct students preserve teachings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٢- كما يرجع الفضل في ذلك أيضًا إلى أحد علماء الجيل الثاني من تلامذته غير المباشرين الذين تلقوا عمَّنْ صحبوا أبا الحسن، وأخذوا عنه، كما أشرنا في الفقرة السابقة الخاصة بالتلاميذ، وأبرزهم، في هذا الصدد، هو «الأستاذ» أبو بكر بن فورك الأصبهاني (٤٠٦هـ)، قرينُ الباقلاني (٤٠٣هـ)، وصاحب الفضل المذكور، والسعي المشكور في تسجيل آراء الإمام الأشعري، وغيره من متكلمي الأشاعرة وأهل السنة، فكان في هذا الأمر كالإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني (١٨٩هـ) في حفظ تراث أبي حنيفة -رضي الله عنه- ومدرسته، وكسحنون (٢٤٠هـ) صاحب المدونة وابن أبي زيد القيرواني (٣٨٦هـ) الذي لُقِّبَ بمالك الصغير، في حفظهما فقه إمام دار الهجرة -رضي الله عنه. وقد نشر المستشرق الفرنسي جيماريه، على نحو طيب - برغم انتقاد بعض الباحثين العرب له - كتاب ابن فورك: مجرد مقالات.
2- Likewise, credit for that also goes to one of the scholars of the second generation of his indirect students who learned from those who accompanied Abu al-Hasan and took from him, as we indicated in the previous paragraph concerning the students. The most prominent of them in this regard is 'al-Ustadh' Abu Bakr ibn Furak al-Isfahani (d. 406 AH), the peer of al-Baqillani (d. 403 AH), who has the mentioned merit and the appreciated effort in recording the views of Imam al-Ash'ari and other Ash'ari theologians and Ahl al-Sunna. He was in this matter like Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH) in preserving the legacy of Abu Hanifa - may Allah be pleased with him - and his school, and like Sahnun (d. 240 AH), author of al-Mudawwana, and Ibn Abi Zayd al-Qayrawani (d. 386 AH), who was nicknamed 'Malik al-Saghir', in their preservation of the jurisprudence of the Imam of the Abode of Hijra - may Allah be pleased with him. The French orientalist Gimaret published Ibn Furak's book 'Mujarrad Maqalat' in a good manner - despite the criticism of some Arab researchers of him.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical and historical account of Ibn Furak's role in preserving the doctrinal legacy of Imam al-Ash'ari. It begins by attributing credit to one of the second-generation students of al-Ash'ari's companions, highlighting Ibn Furak as the most prominent. The passage compares Ibn Furak's efforts to those of earlier figures who preserved the teachings of their respective imams: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani for Abu Hanifa, and Sahnun and Ibn Abi Zayd for Malik. Then it mentions the modern publication of Ibn Furak's work 'Mujarrad Maqalat' by the French orientalist Gimaret, noting that despite criticism, it was done well. The passage emphasises the continuity of scholarly preservation across generations.

Key Terms
ابن فورك
مجرد مقالات
المستشرق جيماريه

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ibn Furak was a direct student of al-Ash'ari.
Correction: Ibn Furak belonged to the second generation of students, learning from those who had accompanied al-Ash'ari, not from al-Ash'ari himself.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ibn Furak's systematic recording of al-Ash'ari's views, akin to earlier preservers, ensured the survival and transmission of the Ash'ari school.

Ibn Furak's Scholarly Compilation and Editorial Approach
Editorial remarks on Ibn Furak's compilation method and classification decision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Ibn Furak's method of preserving early Ash'ari texts from lost sources and the reasoning behind the editor's preliminary classification instead of a repeated list.

Core Idea
Ibn Furak's scholarly instinct preserved threatened texts from lost works.

This passage offers a glimpse into the painstaking work of early Muslim scholars to preserve theological heritage. Ibn Furak, sensing the loss of many of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's books, extracted his views from about 30 now-lost works. He also collected the articles of Ibn Kullab, which remain lost but have been partially reconstructed from later sources. The editor explains why, instead of reciting lists of works, he will provide a preliminary classification.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to understand the content. Note the scholarly context.
2
Identify Ibn Furak's key actions
Notice that Ibn Furak extracted Ash'ari's views from about 30 books that are mostly lost, and he also collected Ibn Kullab's articles. Recognise his scholarly foresight.
3
Understand the fate of Ibn Kullab's articles
The passage states that Ibn Kullab's articles are still lost, but some Moroccan scholars attempted to reconstruct them from Ibn Taymiyya's works.
This shows the fragility of early texts.
4
Grasp the editorial decision
The editor declines to repeat lists of works done by Ibn Furak, Ibn 'Asakir, and others, opting instead for a preliminary classification. Understand why this is a practical choice.
5
Reflect on the scholarly chain
Consider how scholars like Ibn Furak, Ibn 'Asakir, and Ibn Taymiyya contributed to preserving Ash'ari thought across generations.

Source Text
