مقدمة التحقيق. الشيخ أبي الحسن الأشعري، الذي استخلصه -كما سلف ذكره- من نحو ٣٠ كتابًا لأبي الحسن، أكثرها الآن مفقود. كما جمع ابن فورك أيضًا، بحسه العلمي التوثيقي، كأنَّه شعر بالمصير الذي يتهدد كتب الإمام، ومقالاته، ومقالات غيره من أصحابه السابقين واللاحقين من علماء أهل السنة والجماعة، فجمع مقالات ابن كلاب أيضًا، وهي مفقودة ما تزال، وإن حاول بعض علماء المغاربة جمعَها من كتب ابن تيمية الزاخرة بالنصوص ذات الأصل المفقود، وخاصة كتابه الماتع الحافل بالنقول: «درء تعارض العقل والنقل». وفي هذه المقدمة لن نسرد المؤلفات التي نسبت إلى الشيخ، كما حاول هو نفسه - جزاه الله عنا خيرًا - وحاول مؤرخوه وأتباعه من بعده، وخصوصًا حافظ الشام ومؤرخه ابن عساكر في كتاب «التبيين»، فقد أشار إلى القائمة التي ضمنها الإمام كتاب «العمد في الرؤية»، وأضاف إليها ابن فورك مؤلفات الشيخ بعد عام ٣٢٠هـ، واستدرك ابن عساكر على قائمة ابن فورك ثلاثة كتب أخرى. وقد بدا لنا - بدلا من السرد المكرر - أن نقوم بتصنيف تمهيدي لهذه
Introduction to the Investigation. Sheikh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, which he extracted - as previously mentioned - from about 30 books of Abu al-Hasan, most of which are now lost. Ibn Furak also, with his documentary scholarly instinct, as if he sensed the fate that threatened the books of the Imam, his articles, and the articles of others among his predecessors and successors from the scholars of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, so he also collected the articles of Ibn Kullab, which are still lost, although some Moroccan scholars attempted to collect them from Ibn Taymiyya's books rich with texts of lost origin, especially his delightful book full of quotations: 'Dar' Ta'arud al-'Aql wa al-Naql'. And in this introduction we will not list the works attributed to the Sheikh, as he himself tried - may Allah reward him well - and his historians and followers after him tried, especially the Hafiz of Syria and his historian Ibn 'Asakir in the book 'al-Tabyin', for he referred to the list that the Imam included in the book 'al-'Amad fi al-Ru'ya', and Ibn Furak added to it the Sheikh's works after the year 320 AH, and Ibn 'Asakir added three other books to Ibn Furak's list. And it seemed to us - instead of repeated listing - to make a preliminary classification of these
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage constitutes a set of editorial remarks from the introduction. It first describes how Ibn Furak extracted al-Ash'ari's views from about 30 now-lost books, demonstrating his scholarly instinct to preserve threatened material. Then it notes that Ibn Furak similarly collected the articles of Ibn Kullab, which remain lost despite attempts by Moroccan scholars to reconstruct them from Ibn Taymiyya's works. Finally, the editor explains that instead of repeating lists of works attributed to al-Ash'ari, which have been compiled by Ibn Furak and later supplemented by Ibn 'Asakir, they will provide a preliminary classification. The passage highlights the fragility of primary sources and the role of later scholars in reconstructing them.

Six Categories of Ash'ari's Writings
Classification of Ash'ari's works into six categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six categories of Imam al-Ash'ari's writings as classified by purpose and audience, recognizing the breadth of his scholarship beyond polemics.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's works span objective surveys, self-criticism, and legal sciences, not just polemics.

Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari authored a vast number of works—over a hundred according to some accounts. His writings served diverse purposes: from defending his own views to objectively recording others' opinions, refuting specific thinkers, critiquing his own earlier positions, answering questions, and composing works on religious sciences. The passage below, from the introduction to a critical edition of 'Al-Luma', enumerates these six categories, offering a window into Ash'ari's comprehensive scholarly methodology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the numbered categories (1 through 6). Try to grasp the overall structure before diving into details.
2
Identify each category
The passage lists six categories. As you read, highlight or mentally note the distinguishing feature of each: purpose, audience, and content.
Categories 1 and 2 contrast: expressing his own views vs. presenting others' views.
3
Reflect on the self-criticism category
Category 4 is unique: Ash'ari criticized his own earlier Mu'tazili views. Consider what this says about his intellectual honesty.
This is a branch of 'naqd' (refutation).
4
Connect to broader scholarship
Category 6 shows Ash'ari also wrote on usul al-fiqh and tafsir, linking him to the wider Islamic scholarly tradition. Note how this challenges the stereotype that he only engaged in polemics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكتب التي تربو على المئة كتاب أو تبلغ المئات في بعض الروايات، وذلك طبقا لمفاهيم العناوين، والقليل من البيانات التي وردت في وصفها، ممن تيسر لهم الاطلاع عليها قديما، أو على بعضها، وحَرَصُوا على النقل منها ; كابن فورك، والباقلاني، والجويني، وابن السبكي (۷۷۱هـ) ، وابن عساكر (٥٧١هـ) من أعيان مدرسته وكابن تيمية (۷۲۸هـ) ، وابن القيم (٧٥١هـ)، والذهبي (٧٤٨هـ) ، وابن الجوزي (٥٩٧هـ) من غيرهم ; وذلك سعي متواضع نحو تصنيف حقيقي، يعتمد على فحص الكتب، الموجودة الآن، وما قد يكشف عنه البحث المتواصل - إن شاء الله- كما كشف «المجرد»، والحمد لله رب العالمين. عن (۱) فللشيخ كتب عبّر فيها عن آرائه، أو إن شئت آراء أهل السنة والجماعة، مؤيدة ببراهينه هو وأدلته، طبقا لمنهج اتخذه لنفسه، بعد تمحيصه علم الكلام وغربلته وإن لم تخل بطبيعة العرض الكلامي، من آرائه في أقوال الآخرين أحيانًا، لكنها أُلّفَتْ أساسا، لبيان آرائه ومواقفه، الشارحة لمواقف أهل السنة والجماعة . (۲) وله كتب أخرى، أخْلَصَها لعرض آراء الآخرين ومقالاتهم، سجَّلَها بإنصاف وموضوعية، وإن لم تخل من لمحات نقدية قليلة أحيانًا، وميّز فيها بين مقالات غير المسلمين من غير الملة، ومقالات المسلمين أو أهل الملةِ والقبلة، أو المُصلِّين، كما عبّر -رحمه الله- في عنوان كتاب «المقالات». مقدمة التحقيق (۳) وله طائفة أخرى من المؤلفات وجهها إلى مفكرين بأعيانهم، ينقض بها آراءهم المخالفة للصواب في رأيه، أو لفرق ومدارس بعينها ينتقد بعض آرائها . (٤) ومن أفرع كتب «النقض»، نوع طريف، رد فيها على نفسه، عندما كان على الاعتزال يمارس الشيخ فيها نقدا ذاتيا، لا يخلو من شجاعة وإنصاف . (٥) وكتب يجيب فيها عن أسئلة وُجهت إليه في البصرة وبغداد، من بعض أهلها أو جاءته في رسائل، من الأمصار الإسلامية المختلفة، وغير ذلك من المحاورات والإملاءات، والمجادلات الشفوية التي لم تسجل في كتب، ولا وصلنا شيء منها، إلا ما أوردها الديلمي في كتابه عن شيخه ابن خفيف سيرة الشيخ الكبير (٦) وكتب ألفها -رحمه الله- في العلوم الشرعية : كأصول الفقه والتفسير، كما فعل نظراؤه كالماتريدي، والكثيرون من الأشاعرة من بعده، وخصوصا الشافعية منهم، سجلتها كتب «الببليوجرافيا»، وكتب الطبقات وخصوصا ابن السبكي في «طبقات الشافعية»، ويلحق بها كتب الجدل وآدابه; فهو في الأصل من مكملات علم أصول الفقه، ثم استعاره المتكلمون
The books that exceed one hundred or reach hundreds in some narrations, according to the concepts of titles, and the little data that came in their description, from those who were able to see them in the past, or some of them, and were eager to quote from them; such as Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, Ibn al-Subki (771 AH), Ibn ‘Asakir (571 AH) among the notables of his school, and Ibn Taymiyya (728 AH), Ibn al-Qayyim (751 AH), al-Dhahabi (748 AH), Ibn al-Jawzi (597 AH) among others; and that is a humble effort towards a real classification, based on examining the books existing now, and what continuous research may reveal - God willing - as it revealed 'al-Mujarrad', and praise be to God, Lord of the worlds. About (1): For the Shaykh, there are books in which he expressed his views, or if you wish, the views of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a, supported by his own proofs and evidences, according to a method he adopted for himself, after his scrutiny and sifting of kalam, although they are not devoid, by the nature of kalam presentation, of his views on the sayings of others sometimes, but they were authored primarily to explain his views and positions, which explain the positions of Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a. (2) He has other books, which he dedicated to presenting the views of others and their articles, recording them with fairness and objectivity, although they are not devoid of occasional slight critical glances, and he distinguished in them between the articles of non-Muslims from outside the religion, and the articles of Muslims or the people of the religion and the qibla, or the prayers, as he - may God have mercy on him - expressed in the title of the book 'al-Maqalat'. Introduction of the investigation (3) He has another group of writings that he directed to specific thinkers, refuting with them their views that contradict correctness in his opinion, or to specific sects and schools criticizing some of their views. (4) And among the branches of the 'naqd' books, a curious type, in which he refuted himself, when he was upon Mu'tazilism, the Shaykh practiced in them self-criticism, not devoid of courage and fairness. (5) And books in which he answers questions that were directed to him in Basra and Baghdad, from some of its people, or came to him in letters from various Islamic regions, and other dialogues, dictations, and oral debates that were not recorded in books, and none of which has reached us, except what al-Daylami recorded in his book about his shaykh Ibn Khafif, 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir'. (6) And books he authored - may God have mercy on him - in the religious sciences: such as usul al-fiqh and tafsir, as his counterparts like al-Maturidi and many of the Ash'aris after him did, especially the Shafi'is among them, recorded by the bibliography books and the class books, especially Ibn al-Subki in 'Tabaqat al-Shafi'iyya', and to these are attached the books of debate and its etiquette; for it is originally a completion of the science of usul al-fiqh, then the mutakallimun borrowed it.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the literary output of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari, as presented in the introduction to the critical edition of 'Al-Luma'. The passage begins by noting the vast number of his works—over a hundred, even hundreds according to some accounts—and mentions later scholars who relied on them, both from his own school (Ibn Furak, al-Baqillani, al-Juwayni, Ibn al-Subki, Ibn ‘Asakir) and others (Ibn Taymiyya, Ibn al-Qayyim, al-Dhahabi, Ibn al-Jawzi). Then it proceeds to enumerate six categories of his writings based on purpose and audience:

1. Books expressing his own views (or those of Ahl al-Sunna) with his proofs, after having scrutinized kalam. These primarily clarify his positions, though they sometimes include critiques of others.
2. Books dedicated to objectively presenting the views of others, distinguishing between non-Muslims and Muslims. The work 'al-Maqalat' is given as an example.
3. Books refuting specific thinkers or groups, directed against their erroneous views.
4. A curious subset of refutation works where he criticized his own earlier Mu'tazili positions, showing self-criticism and fairness.
5. Books that answer questions sent to him from Basra, Baghdad, and other regions, as well as records of oral debates that have not survived except for those preserved by al-Daylami.
6. Books on religious sciences (usul al-fiqh, tafsir, etc.), similar to the works of al-Maturidi and later Ash'aris. He also notes that books on jadal (debate) and its etiquette, originally part of usul al-fiqh, were later adopted by mutakallimun.

This classification demonstrates the breadth of Ash'ari's scholarship, moving beyond polemics to include objective reporting, self-reflection, and positive theological and legal instruction.

Key Terms
أهل السنة والجماعة
المقالات
النقض
الجدل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Ash'ari only wrote polemical works defending his own views.
Correction: The passage shows he also wrote objective surveys, self-criticism, and legal works, demonstrating a wider range of scholarly interests.

Checkpoint
Which category of Ash'ari's books includes works where he criticizes his own earlier Mu'tazili views?
A) Books expressing his own views
B) Books presenting others' views
C) Books refuting specific thinkers
D) Self-refutation books (a branch of naqd)

Key Takeaway
Ash'ari's literary output was diverse, encompassing not only polemics but also objective surveys, self-criticism, and contributions to religious sciences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Ash'ari's First Group of Theological Works
Enumerating Ash'ari's first group of theological books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the classification and significance of Imam al-Ash'ari's earliest theological writings that represent his mature positions.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's first group of works establishes his mature theological methodology.

This passage from a biographical source catalogues the first group of Imam al-Ash'ari's theological books. These works represent his developed Ash'ari positions on key issues like divine attributes, faith, and hermeneutics. The list shows the breadth of his scholarship and the systematic organization of his thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the books
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. List all the book titles mentioned as belonging to the first group. Note that some are described with their content.
Pay attention to the order: the passage starts with al-Musannaf and ends with al-Funun.
2
Understand the principle on attributes
The passage repeats the Ash'ari principle on divine attributes: necessary ta'wil is not required; the default is to accept the apparent meaning unless it leads to anthropomorphism. Notice that this principle is exemplified by the content of al-Musannaf.
This connects back to earlier lessons on the Ash'ari approach to attributes.
3
Count the books and see the grouping
Follow the passage as it counts books: initially eight, then eleven. Recognize that the grouping is based on expressing Ash'ari's own views, even when refuting opponents. This shows a deliberate classification.
The passage mentions footnotes but focus on the main argument.

Source Text

ففي كتاب «المُصنفِ»، وهو من أكبر كتبه الثلاثةِ في التفسير، فالمُختزَنُ هو أكبرها على الإطلاق، والمصنف يتلوه، يثبت الشيخ -رحمه الله - الوجه واليدين والاستواء والموقف العام للأشاعرة كما أسلفنا آنفا - ليس هو وجوب التأويل، بل الأصلُ عدمه، والوقوف مع الظاهر، إلا إذا أدّى الظاهر، لسبب أو لآخر، إلى تشبيه أو تمثيل أو تجسیم، كما حدث في تاريخ المذهب الحنبلي فعلا (۱)، واضطر المعاصرون لهم من شيوخه المحققين الرد على هؤلاء المشبهة، وإلى دَفْع شُبه من شبه وتمرد ونسب ذلك إلى السيد الجليل الإمام أحمد»، كما هو ثابت معلوم، هذا، مع أن كتاب «الصفات الكبير»، وهو من أوسع كتب أبي الحسن الكلاميَّة، قد كتب نقدا ذاتيا لمؤلفات الأشعري في نصرة الاعتزال، ويمكن عده من هذا النوع الأول أيضًا، وإذا احتسبناه مع الإبانة صار معنا - في المجموعة -الأولى ثمانية كتب. (۱) انظر كتاب ابن خزيمة الذي أسماه كتاب التوحيد وإثبات صفات الرب عز وجل، وفيه يورد الأعضاء المتشابهة، كما لو كان يصف إنسانا، بدءًا بالعينين نزولا إلى القدمين. وأنكره شيوخ المذهب للتشبيه والتجسيم الغليظ الذي يحتويه واضطر للاعتذار عنه وبعده صدرت عن الحنابلة سلسلة من الكتب لتنزيه مذهب الإمام أحمد عن هذه الطامة الكبرى. ومن هذه المجموعة الأولى أيضًا كتاب كبير، كما يقول ابن عساكر (۱) في اختلاف الناس في الأسماء والأحكام والخاص والعام وهو يُعبّر عن مواقفه الخاصة، من المؤوّل، والظاهر، والمحكم والمتشابه، ويشرح مصطلحات كلامية أخرى كان يعبر عنها بالأسماء والأحكام كالإسلام والإيمان، ومرتكب الكبيرة، ونحوها؛ فهو بين الكلام وأصول الفقه، وهو في بيان أقواله أصلا، وإن احتوى أيضًا مقارنتها بأقوال المخالفين في هذه الأمور، كما هو الشأن عادة، فيمكن لهذا عده من هذه المجموعة الأولى المعبّرة عن آراء الشيخ الكلامية، ومواقفه، أصلا، وإن احتوت الرد على المخالفين على وجه الإجمال. (۱) انظر ابن عساكر: تبيين كذب المفتري ص ۱۳۰ وما بعدها، وانظر أيضًا السبكي: طبقات، ٣٦١/٢. ومنها أيضًا كتاب: النوادر في دقيق الكلام، وقد ذيَّله بكتاب آخر سماه «النوادر في فنون من لطائف الكلام، ويتضح من أسمائها أنها تنتمي إلى هذه المجموعة الأولى، فمعنا الآن أحدَ عَشَرَ كتابًا، من المجموعة الأولى. وقد يعد في مؤلفاته الكلامية، التي يعبر فيها عن نفسه: كتابه في «المعارف» كما أسماه وهو متعلق بالجانب المنهجي، الذي يذكر ضمن باب الأمور العامة) من كتب علم الكلام (۲). وكتاب الفنون» في أبواب من الكلام، ويبدو أنه غير كتابه
Thus in the book 'Al-Musannaf' – which is one of his three largest works in tafsir, 'Al-Mukhtazan' being the largest of all, followed by 'Al-Musannaf' – the Shaykh (may Allah have mercy on him) affirms the Face, the Hands, and Istiwa' and the general position of the Ash'aris as we mentioned earlier: it is not that ta'wil is obligatory, but the default is its absence, and stopping with the apparent meaning, unless the apparent meaning leads, for one reason or another, to tashbih, tamthil, or tajsim – as actually happened in the history of the Hanbali school (1), and the contemporary verifying scholars among them were compelled to refute these anthropomorphists and to repel the doubts of those who doubted and rebelled, attributing that to the noble master Imam Ahmad, as is well established. Moreover, while the book 'Al-Sifat al-Kabir' – which is among the broadest of Abu al-Hasan's theological works – was written as a self-critique of al-Ash'ari's writings in support of Mu'tazilism, it can also be counted in this first type, and if we include it together with 'Al-Ibanah', we have eight books in the first group. (1) See the book of Ibn Khuzaymah which he named 'Kitab al-Tawhid wa Ithbat Sifat al-Rabb', in which he lists the similar body parts as if describing a human, starting from the eyes down to the feet. The school's scholars rejected it for the gross tashbih and tajsim it contained, and he was compelled to apologize for it, and afterwards a series of books were issued by the Hanbalis to exonerate the school of Imam Ahmad from this great calamity. Also from this first group is a large book, as Ibn 'Asakir says (1), on the disagreement of people regarding names and judgments, the specific and the general, and it expresses his own positions on the mu'awwal (allegorically interpreted), the dhahir (apparent), the muhkam (clear), and the mutashabih (ambiguous), and it explains other theological terms he used to express by 'names and judgments', such as Islam, faith, and the committer of major sins, and the like. Thus it lies between kalam and usul al-fiqh, and it is primarily an exposition of his own views, although it also contains comparisons with the views of opponents on these matters, as is usual. So it can be counted in this first group – that which expresses the Shaykh's theological views and positions – even though it contains refutations of opponents in an overall manner. (1) See Ibn 'Asakir, Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari, p. 130ff., and also al-Subki, Tabaqat, 2/361. Also among them is the book 'Al-Nawadir fi Daqiq al-Kalam', and he appended to it another book he named 'Al-Nawadir fi Funun min Lata'if al-Kalam', and it is clear from their names that they belong to this first group. So now we have eleven books from the first group. Also counted among his theological works in which he expresses himself is his book 'Al-Ma'arif' as he named it, which is related to the methodological aspect, mentioned under the general principles (al-umur al-'amma) of kalam books (2). And the book 'Al-Funun in the chapters of kalam, and it seems it is different from his other book
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the first group of Imam al-Ash'ari's theological writings. It begins by mentioning 'Al-Musannaf' (a major tafsir work) and reiterates the Ash'ari principle on attributes (from the previous lesson) as an example of the content. It then notes that 'Al-Sifat al-Kabir' is a self-critique of his earlier pro-Mu'tazilite writings, and together with 'Al-Ibanah' it yields eight books in this group. The passage then introduces a large book by Ibn 'Asakir (actually it is Ash'ari's own book? The text says 'as Ibn 'Asakir says' – it might be a book by Ash'ari that Ibn 'Asakir writes about; context suggests it is Ash'ari's book) on names and judgments, which covers terminology like Islam, faith, grave sins, and lies between kalam and usul al-fiqh. Next, 'Al-Nawadir fi Daqiq al-Kalam' and its supplement are added, bringing the count to eleven. Finally, two more books are mentioned: 'Al-Ma'arif' (methodological) and 'Al-Funun' (on chapters of kalam). The passage thus gives a detailed catalog of Ash'ari's works in his first group, which represent his own developed positions.

?

Life of Imam al-Ashari
beginner
4 min
Imam al-Ash'ari's First Group of Works
Editor lists Ash'ari's first group of works, totaling twenty books.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the extent and thematic variety of Imam al-Ash'ari's early writings in theology and methodology, as enumerated by the editor.

Core Idea
Imam al-Ash'ari authored at least twenty major works in his first group alone, covering refutations, epistemology, and theological method.

This lesson introduces the first group of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's works as listed by the editor. The list reveals the breadth of his writings, including books on refuting heretical sects, theological methodology, and rational inquiry. Understanding this corpus helps situate Ash'ari as a prolific scholar whose works laid the foundation for Ash'arite theology.

Guided Path
1
Read the full list of books
Read the Arabic passage carefully, noting the titles mentioned and the final count of twenty books. Pay attention to the descriptions of each work.
The editor provides details about several key books, especially Al-Ihtijaj and Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth.
2
Identify thematic clusters
Notice that some books focus on refuting deviant sects (e.g., Al-Luma', Al-Funun, Al-Jawhar), while others deal with theological methodology (e.g., Al-Ihtijaj, Al-Hathth, Risala ila Ahl al-Thaghr). The last one addresses human incapacity.
This shows Ash'ari's concern with both polemics and foundational method.
3
Focus on Al-Ihtijaj
This book is described as discussing rational argumentation against the Mu'tazilites, particularly the analogy of the unseen to the witnessed. It divides analogy into four types. Understand the importance of this work for Ash'ari's methodology.
The four types: shared genus/reality, shared cause, shared evidence, shared condition.
4
Examine the epistle to Ahl al-Thaghr
This epistle affirms a key principle: the invalidity of a proof does not invalidate the intended meaning. Note that later Ash'aris like al-Baqillani followed this, and Ibn Taymiyya praised Ash'ari for it. It also asserts the obligation of rational reflection for every morally responsible person.
5
Reflect on the book on human incapacity
This work argues that incapacity for something does not imply incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity only arises from an existent. Consider how this ties into Ash'ari's views on human agency and divine power.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللمع في الرد على أَهْلِ الزَّيْغِ والبِدَع
الفنون في الرد على الملحدين، وكلاهما يأتي ضمن هذه المجموعة الأولى، وبهما تصبح هذه المجموعة أربعة عشر كتابًا. وكتاب آخر، لا نعرف إلا عنوانه: «الجوهر في الرد على أهل الزيغ والمنكر»، وغالب الظن أنه من هذه المجموعة، وبه يبلغ عددها خمسة عشر كتابًا.
- وكتاب الاحتجاج وقد يُسمَّى أيضًا كتاب الاستشهاد وعنوانه يشي بأنه في المنهج الكلامي، والمراد به الاحتجاج والاستدلال العقلي؛ فهو يناقش قول المعتزلة أساسا بقياس «الغائب على الشاهد»، ويُلزِمُهم بعدم الموضوعية في تطبيقه، ولو أجرَوْه على وجهه لاعترفوا بكلِّ الصفات الإلهية، ويذكر تفاصيل يظن أنها لتلاميذه؛ فهو يقسمه الأقسام الأربعة أو الأشكال الأربعة: القياس بجامع الحد والحقيقة، وبجامع العلة وبجامع الدليل وبجامع الشرط.
- ومنها كتاب الحث على البحث وهو في المنهج الكلامي والنظر العقلي، وهو يطابق استحسان الخوض في علم الكلام الذي شكك فيه بعض الباحثين، قديمًا وحديثًا، في مصر وخارجها، وهو في رأيي تشكيك في غير محله؛ لأنه ليس قائما على الآليات المنهجية العلمية، بل على الميول والاتجاهات المذهبية، التي تهدف إلى رسم صورة حرفية ظاهرية للشيخ أبي الحسن، لا تتوافق مع ما خلَّفه الرجل من تراث فكري.
- ومنها أيضًا: رسالته إلى أهل الثغر، وهي تؤكد موقفه المنهجي من عدم بطلان المدلول لبطلان دليله كما ذهب إليه الباقلاني وغيره فيما بعد، ويثني ابن تيمية على الأشعري، مشيرًا إلى موقف متأخري الأشاعرة المخالفين لإمامهم في رأيه، والشيخ يؤكد فيها وجوب النظر العقلي على كل مُكَلَّف.
- ومنها كتابه في العجز البشري: يقرر فيه أنَّ العجز عن شيء ليس بالضرورة عجزا عن ضده، وأن العجز لا يكون إلا من الموجود. فهذه عشرون كتابًا تمامًا. والحمد لله رب العالمين.
Al-Luma' fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Bida' [The Glimmers in Refuting the People of Deviation and Innovation], Al-Funun fi al-Radd 'ala al-Mulhidin [The Arts in Refuting the Atheists], and both come within this first group, and by them this group becomes fourteen books. And another book, of which we know only its title: 'Al-Jawhar fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Munkar' [The Jewel in Refuting the People of Deviation and Denial], and most likely it is from this group, and by it its number reaches fifteen books. - And the book 'Al-Ihtijaj' [The Argumentation] and it may also be called 'Kitab al-Istishhad' [The Book of Testimony] and its title indicates that it is in the theological methodology, and by it is meant rational argumentation and proof; for it discusses the Mu'tazilites' statement primarily by analogy of the unseen to the witnessed, and makes them liable for lack of objectivity in their application, and if they had applied it properly they would have acknowledged all the divine attributes. And it mentions details that are thought to be for his students; for he divides it into four divisions or four forms: analogy by shared genus and reality, analogy by shared cause, analogy by shared evidence, and analogy by shared condition. - And among them is the book 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth' [Urging Investigation] which is on theological methodology and rational reflection, and it corresponds to the approval of engaging in the science of kalam which some researchers have doubted, both ancient and modern, in Egypt and abroad, and in my opinion it is doubt misplaced; because it is not based on scientific methodological mechanisms, but on sectarian tendencies and orientations, which aim to draw a literal superficial picture of Shaykh Abi al-Hasan, that is not consistent with the intellectual legacy he left. - And among them also: his 'Risala ila Ahl al-Thaghr' [Epistle to the People of the Frontier], which affirms his methodological position regarding the invalidity of the indication not being invalidated by the invalidity of its proof, as al-Baqillani and others later held, and Ibn Taymiyya praises al-Ash'ari, pointing to the position of the later Ash'aris who opposed their imam in his opinion, and the Shaykh affirms in it the obligation of rational reflection upon every morally responsible person. - And among them is his book on human incapacity: in which he establishes that incapacity for something is not necessarily incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity comes only from the existent. So these are twenty books exactly. And praise be to God, Lord of the worlds.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is from the editor's introduction, listing the first group of Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's works. The editor begins by mentioning two books: 'Al-Luma'' and 'Al-Funun', which are part of the first group, making the group fourteen books. Then he adds another book, 'Al-Jawhar', making fifteen. Then he describes 'Al-Ihtijaj' (also called 'Al-Istishhad'), explaining its content about theological methodology and refutation of Mu'tazilites using analogy of the unseen to the witnessed. He notes that if applied properly, it would lead to acknowledgment of all divine attributes. He mentions that the book is divided into four types of analogy: by shared genus and reality, shared cause, shared evidence, and shared condition. Next, he describes 'Al-Hathth 'ala al-Bahth', defending engaging in kalam against skeptics, criticizing those who doubt it as being motivated by sectarian bias rather than scientific methodology. Then he mentions 'Risala ila Ahl al-Thaghr', which affirms that the invalidity of a proof does not imply the invalidity of the intended meaning—a point later expanded by al-Baqillani and praised by Ibn Taymiyya. In this epistle, Ash'ari asserts the obligation of rational inquiry upon every morally responsible person. Finally, he mentions a book on human incapacity, arguing that incapacity for something does not entail incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity arises only from an existent. The editor concludes that these total twenty books.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You are commanded to engage in rational reflection about your Creator. When have you avoided deep thought about Allah's attributes because it felt uncomfortable? What would it take for you to shoulder that obligation today?
?
The book on human incapacity teaches that being unable to do something does not make you unable to do its opposite. Where in your life have you used 'I can't' as an excuse when really you were unwilling to try? What step will you take this week to act on what you are actually capable of?
?
Al-Ash'ari shows that if the Mu'tazilites had applied their method objectively, they would have acknowledged all of Allah's attributes. In what area of your understanding of Allah might you be applying inconsistent standards? What would it mean to be truly objective in your faith?

Al-Ash'ari's Works: Refutation and Doxography
Editor classifies al-Ash'ari's works into two types: refutation and doxography.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main categories of al-Ash'ari's works: refutation works and doxographical works, and the characteristics of each.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's works are either refutations or objective doxographies.

This editorial passage from the introduction to al-Luma' provides a valuable classification of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari's extensive corpus. The editor distinguishes between two broad types: works of refutation and argumentation, and works of articles (maqalat) that document and analyze theological schools. This classification helps us appreciate al-Ash'ari's dual role as a polemicist and a pioneering historian of ideas.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the overall classification.
Pay attention to the transition between the two types.
2
Identify the first type
The passage first mentions works of refutation and argumentation. Note the examples: the letter to the people of al-Thaghr and the book on human incapacity.
The editor highlights key methodological points from these works.
3
Identify the second type
The second type is 'books of articles' (kutub al-maqalat), covering the history of theological and philosophical schools.
Understand its resemblance to modern comparative religion.
4
Notice the editor's remarks
The editor corrects Sezgin's error regarding 'Jumal al-Maqalat' and comments on the objective methodology.
This shows the importance of careful scholarly attribution.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و-منها أيضًا : رسالته إلى أهل الثغر ، وهي تؤكد موقفه المنهجي ، من عدم بطلان المدلول لبطلان دليله كما ذهب إليه الباقلاني وغيره فيما بعد، ويثني ابن تيمية على الأشعري، مشيرًا إلى موقف متأخري الأشاعرة المخالفين لإمامهم في رأيه، والشيخ يؤكد فيها وجوب النظر العقلي على كل مُكَلَّف . - ومنها كتابه في العجز البشري : يقرر فيه أنَّ العجز عن شيء ليس بالضرورة عجزا عن ضده، وأن العجز لا يكون إلا من الموجود . فهذه عشرون كتابًا تمامًا . والحمد لله رب العالمين . ٢ - أما النوع الثاني من مؤلفاته : وهي كتب المقالات، أو تاريخ الأفكار والمذاهب الكلامية ،والفلسفية سواء ما كان منها داخل المِلَّةِ الإسلامية أو خارجها، فتلك طائفة كبيرة من كتبه، تشمل ما عُرِفَ حديثًا بتاريخ الأديان» أو «مقارنة الأديان»، وهو ما عُرِفَ اللُّمَع في الردّ على أَهلِ الزَّيْغِ والبدع لدينا منذ ابن حزم (٤٥٦هـ) ، والشهرستاني (٥٤٨هـ)، والرازي (٦٠٦هـ) ، بعلم الملل والنحل»، وقد أرسى له الشيخ منهجًا موضوعيًا أشرنا إليه فيما سبق في مقدمة كتاب «مقالات الإسلاميين . وكتاب المقالات ليس هو آخر مؤلفاته، بل ربما كان أول أو من أوائل - مؤلفاته بعد التحول عن الاعتزال، وقد اشترط فيه ألا ينسب إلى أي رجل أو فريق أقوال الآخرين عنه ، بل ما يعبر به هو عن نفسه ورأيه : والكتاب - بوجه عام - دُرَّة من دُرَرِ التراث الكلامي والفكري والإنساني، في ماضينا الزاهر، الذي لم ينل حقه من الدرس والتحليل . - ومنها كتاب في اختصار الكتاب السابق، بعنوان: «جُمَلُ المقالات، وقد أخطأ «سيزجين»، على خبرته الواسعة؛ إذ اعتبر «المجرَّد) تلخيصًا لكتاب مقالات الإسلاميين» ، وإنما تلخيصه في هذه «الجُمَل) ، التي لم نعثر عليها بعد - وهو لا يمنع في باب المقالات» والمذاهب أن يُحكم بمذهب على مذهب آخر بعد مقارنة أدلتهما، ولذا ردَّ -رحمه الله -
And among them also: his letter to the people of al-Thaghr, which affirms his methodological stance that the invalidating of the proof does not entail the invalidating of the proven meaning, as al-Baqillani and others later held. Ibn Taymiyyah praises al-Ash'ari, pointing to the position of later Ash'aris who oppose their imam in his opinion. And the shaykh affirms in it the obligation of rational reflection (al-nazar al-'aqli) upon every legally responsible person. And among them is his book on human incapacity: he states in it that incapacity for something is not necessarily incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity only comes from the existent. So these are twenty complete books. Praise be to God, Lord of the worlds. 2. As for the second type of his works: they are the books of articles (kutub al-maqalat), or the history of ideas and theological and philosophical schools, whether they are within the Islamic community or outside it. That is a large group of his books, encompassing what is known recently as 'history of religions' or 'comparative religions,' and it is what has been known as 'Al-Luma' in refutation of the people of deviation and innovation' available to us since Ibn Hazm (456 AH), al-Shahrastani (548 AH), and al-Razi (606 AH), as the science of sects and creeds ('ilm al-milal wa al-nihal). And the shaykh established for it an objective methodology that we have previously referred to in the introduction to the book 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin.' The book of articles is not his last work; rather, it may be the first or among the first of his works after his turning away from Mu'tazilism. He stipulated in it that he should not attribute to any man or group the statements of others, but rather he expresses his own self and opinion. And the book—generally speaking—is a gem among the gems of theological, intellectual, and human heritage in our glorious past, which has not received its due of study and analysis. And among them is a book summarizing the previous one, titled 'Jumal al-Maqalat.' 'Sezgin,' despite his vast expertise, erred in considering 'al-Mujarrad' a summary of the book 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin'; rather, its summary is in these 'al-Jumal,' which we have not yet found. And it does not prevent, in the domain of articles and schools, that one school be judged over another after comparing their proofs. Hence he—may God have mercy on him—refuted...
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a classification of al-Ash'ari's works into two types by the editor of the book. It begins by listing examples from the first type: the letter to the people of al-Thaghr and the book on human incapacity. The letter emphasizes that the invalidity of a proof does not invalidate the proven meaning—a methodological point later supported by al-Baqillani and criticized by Ibn Taymiyyah. It also affirms the obligation of rational reflection (nazar) for every accountable person. The second example, the book on human incapacity, argues that incapacity for one thing does not imply incapacity for its opposite, and that incapacity only proceeds from an existent cause. The editor then concludes the first type with 'these are twenty complete books.' The second type is introduced as 'books of articles' (kutub al-maqalat), which cover the history of theological and philosophical schools both inside and outside Islam, corresponding to modern 'history of religions' or 'comparative religion.' Among these is 'al-Luma'' (the present work), and the editor notes that the shaykh established an objective methodology for this genre, previously mentioned in the introduction to 'Maqalat al-Islamiyyin.' That book may be al-Ash'ari's first after leaving Mu'tazilism, and he insisted on not attributing others' views to anyone but himself. The editor then mentions a condensed version, 'Jumal al-Maqalat,' correcting Sezgin's misattribution. Finally, he notes that in works on sects, one may judge between schools after comparing proofs, and al-Ash'ari did so.

العجز البشري
كتب المقالات
تاريخ الأفكار والمذاهب الكلامية
علم الملل والنحل
مقالات الإسلاميين
جُمَل المقالات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think al-Ash'ari only wrote polemical refutations.
Correction: He also produced objective doxographical works, pioneering the study of sects and creeds.

Checkpoint
According to the editor, what is the second type of al-Ash'ari's works?
A) Books of refutation and argumentation
B) Books of articles (maqalat) on sects and ideas
C) Books on jurisprudence
D) Books on hadith criticism

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's writings are divided into refutation works and doxographical works, with the latter representing a groundbreaking contribution to the objective study of religious sects.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you discuss a belief you disagree with, do you strive to represent it fairly as al-Ash'ari did, or do you rush to refute it? What would change if you first accurately understood the other's perspective?
?
The passage calls al-Ash'ari's doxographical works a 'gem' that hasn't received its due. Are there aspects of Islamic intellectual heritage that you have neglected? What one step can you take this week to study a primary text from a scholar you have overlooked?
?
Al-Ash'ari did not shy away from judging between schools after comparing proofs. Are you willing to evaluate your own views with the same rigor, or do you hold onto positions without critical examination? What is one belief you might re-examine in light of evidence?

Al-Ash'ari's Refutational Works: A Threefold Classification
Editor classifies al-Ash'ari's refutations into three subcategories and lists first subcategory examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's refutational works are classified into three subcategories and identify the specific opponents addressed in the first subcategory.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari refuted not only sects but also individuals and even his own former self.

This passage from the editor of al-Luma' provides a valuable classification of al-Ash'ari's refutational writings. It shows that his polemical output was systematic, targeting three levels: individual scholars, entire sects, and even his own earlier Mu'tazilite positions. The first subcategory demonstrates his engagement with specific contemporary and predecessor thinkers.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification overview
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the overall structure: the third type of al-Ash'ari's works is refutational, subdivided into three sections.
Notice the editor's remark that this type includes most of al-Ash'ari's writings.
2
Understand the tripartite division
Identify the three subcategories: refutation of individual scholars, refutation of sects/currents, and refutation of his own former Mu'tazilite self.
The third subcategory is described as rare in intellectual history.
3
Examine examples from the first subcategory
Review the list of books refuting specific individuals: al-Jubba'i, al-Balkhi, Ibn al-Rawandi, and al-Khalidi (multiple works).
Note the topics covered: divine attributes, interpretation of evidences, will, and vision of Allah.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why al-Ash'ari would refute his own former positions and how this classification shows the breadth of his polemical engagement.

As for the third type: it comprises the books of refutation and invalidation of the statements of opponents, individuals or groups, against Ahl al-Sunnah wa al-Jama‘ah. It includes most of the Imam's (may Allah have mercy on him) writings – whether before the year twenty of the fourth century, or in the last four years of his life – as Ibn ‘Asakir narrates from Ibn Furak. This third type is itself divided into three sections: first, the refutation of the opinions of some individuals among his contemporaries or predecessors from among the opposing scholars; the second section is directed at refuting the doctrines and statements of opposing sects or currents; and the last section – which is rare and unusual in intellectual history – is that by which al-Ash‘ari refutes himself, i.e., the Mu‘tazilite al-Ash‘ari. For he was the tongue of the people in assemblies and their pen in authorship as well. (1) See Ibn ‘Asakir, Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari, p. 131. (2) Ibid., p. 133. Al-Luma‘ fi al-Radd ‘ala Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Bida‘. From the first section: a book refuting the book 'al-Usul' by al-Jubba’i the elder, his former teacher, in which he exposed his obfuscation in all areas of theological thought, especially divine attributes. – And a book refuting the book of al-Balkhi (d. 327 AH) on the interpretation of evidences, containing a methodological discussion of theological inference and refutation of al-Balkhi’s opinions in this regard. – And a third book: refuting the book of Ibn al-Rawandi on 'Attributes and the Qur’an', who is the well-known heretic, who was a Mu‘tazilite and left Mu‘tazilism. – And a book refuting a book of al-Khalidi al-Mu‘tazili, also on 'Attributes and the Qur’an'. – And a book refuting a book of al-Khalidi on 'Will', and that He, glorified be He, willed what was and what was not, and He did not will its existence nor its non-existence, rather it is perpetual non-existence. – And another book refuting a third book of al-Khalidi, previously mentioned in the articles under the title 'al-Muhadhdhab', so he wrote 'al-Dafi‘ li al-Muhadhdhab' on articles and opinions. – And another book, in which he refutes a fourth book in which al-Khalidi denied the vision of Allah, exalted be He, with eyes, in this world and the Hereafter.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a classification by the editor of the third type of al-Ash‘ari’s writings, namely his refutational works. The editor begins by describing this type as comprising books that refute and invalidate the statements of opponents, whether individuals or groups, against Ahl al-Sunnah. He notes that this type includes most of the Imam’s works, both from his early period (before 320 AH) and his last four years. Then he subdivides this type into three sections: (1) refuting opinions of individual scholars from among his contemporaries or predecessors; (2) refuting doctrines of opposing sects or currents; (3) a rare section where al-Ash‘ari refutes his own former Mu‘tazilite self. The editor adds that al-Ash‘ari was the spokesperson and writer for the Mu‘tazila before his conversion. He then proceeds to list examples from the first section: a refutation of al-Jubba’i’s 'al-Usul' on divine attributes; a refutation of al-Balkhi’s work on interpretation of evidences; a refutation of Ibn al-Rawandi’s book on attributes and the Qur’an; multiple refutations of al-Khalidi’s works on various topics including attributes, will, and the vision of Allah. The passage systematically illustrates al-Ash‘ari’s engagement with specific opponents.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Ash'ari had the courage to refute his own former beliefs and writings publicly. Is there a belief or habit you once held that you now know is wrong but have been too proud or afraid to publicly abandon? What would it cost you to repudiate it, and is that cost greater than the cost of remaining in falsehood?
?
The passage shows al-Ash'ari's systematic refutation of individuals including his own teacher. Are you willing to critically examine the teachings of those you respect, or do you accept them blindly out of loyalty? What would you do if you discovered a teacher you admire was mistaken on a matter of truth?
?
Al-Ash'ari devoted much of his life to refuting falsehood, even writing multiple books against a single opponent. How seriously do you take the duty to correct falsehood? Do you avoid difficult discussions, or do you engage with those who disagree with you thoroughly and patiently?

Al-Ash'ari's Refutations of Mu'tazila on Key Issues
List of al-Ash'ari's books refuting Mu'tazila on ru'ya, tajsim, and a Mu'tazili summary.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the range of al-Ash'ari's refutations of Mu'tazila, focusing on vision, anthropomorphism, and his critique of their summary work.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari wrote multiple works targeting specific Mu'tazili doctrines, showing his systematic refutation strategy.

This passage lists several of al-Ash'ari's books that directly refute Mu'tazili positions. These works cover the vision of God, the issue of anthropomorphism, and a detailed refutation of a Mu'tazili compendium on tawhid and justice. Understanding this helps us appreciate the breadth of al-Ash'ari's engagement with his opponents, as he tailored separate works to different doctrinal challenges.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the names of the books and what they refute.
The passage lists four works, but the third is mentioned as 'another book on the meaning of body'.
2
Identify the targets of each work
For each book, note whether it is directed against the Mu'tazila, the Mujassima (Anthropomorphists), or both. The second book critiques both groups.
Al-Ash'ari highlights a weakness in the Mu'tazila regarding anthropomorphism.
3
Reflect on the strategy
Consider why al-Ash'ari wrote separate books on specific issues rather than one comprehensive work. What does this tell us about his method of refutation?
This shows a focused, issue-by-issue approach to theological debate.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب جواز رؤية الله -تعالى- بالأبصار»، نقض فيه كل اعتلالات المعتزلة ضد رؤية الله تعالى في الآخرة. وكتاب الرد على المجسمة»، وكتاب آخرُ في معنى الجسم)) بين فيه عَجْزَ المعتزلة عن الرد على المجسمة . وكتاب نقض فيه كتاب المختصر في التوحيد والعدل للمعتزلة، تكلَّم فيه على «الرؤية» وسائر الصفات، وأبواب القدر، قال عنه : «سألناهم فيه عن مسائل كثيرة أي المعتزلة - ضاقوا بالجواب عنها ذَرْعًا . . . » (١)
The book 'The Permissibility of Seeing God -Exalted- with Eyes', in which he refuted all the arguments of the Mu'tazila against seeing God (ru'yat Allah) in the Hereafter. And the book 'The Refutation of the Anthropomorphists (al-Mujassima)', and another book on the meaning of 'body' (al-jism), in which he explained the inability of the Mu'tazila to refute the Anthropomorphists. And a book in which he refuted the book 'al-Mukhtasar fi al-Tawhid wa al-'Adl' of the Mu'tazila, in which he discussed 'vision' (al-ru'ya) and the rest of the attributes (sifat), and the chapters on predestination (al-qadar). He said about it: 'We asked them therein about many issues, and the Mu'tazila were straitened in answering them...' (1)
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage lists three of al-Ash'ari's works targeting Mu'tazili positions. The first book, 'The Permissibility of Seeing God with Eyes', refutes Mu'tazili arguments against the beatific vision in the afterlife. The second book is against the Anthropomorphists (Mujassima), but al-Ash'ari notes that the Mu'tazila themselves were unable to refute the Mujassima effectively, implying a weakness in their position. The third book is a refutation of a Mu'tazili summary work on tawhid and justice, covering key topics like vision, attributes, and predestination. Al-Ash'ari quotes himself as saying that the Mu'tazila were so pressed by his questions that they could not answer them. The footnote (1) refers to Ibn 'Asakir's work on al-Muftari.

Al-Ash'ari's Books of Scattered Issues
Listing of al-Ash'ari's two works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that al-Ash'ari authored two collections of disputations with Mu'tazila from Basra and Baghdad, known as the Scattered Issues.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's 'Scattered Issues' record his debates with Mu'tazila.

In this lesson, we explore two of al-Ash'ari's important works that document his theological discussions with the Mu'tazila. These books provide a window into his method of argumentation and help establish his independent position.

Guided Path
1
Read the names of the two books
The passage names 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Basriyya' and 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Baghdadiyya'. Notice the adjectives relating to the cities.
'Masa'il al-Manthura' means 'scattered issues'.
2
Understand the context of each book
The Basran book involves issues with the Mu'tazila of Basra; the Baghdadi one with those of Baghdad. This shows al-Ash'ari engaged with both major centers.
3
Reflect on the significance
These works show that al-Ash'ari actively debated his opponents, demonstrating his intellectual independence.

وكتابه الذي أسماه : المسائل المنثورة البصرية»، في مسائل أثيرت ت بينه وبين معتزلة البصرة، ومثله كتاب المسائل المنثورة البغدادية» في مسائل أُثيرَتْ مع البغداديين منهم، الذين يزعم بعضُ المستشرقين أنه كان يخافهم ويجاملهم، وأنه غير بعض أقواله لِيُوافِقَهم، وهذا الكتاب مع الروايات المباشرة لابن خفيف -في كتاب سيرة الشيخ الكبير عن مواجهاته المحتَدِمَةِ مع هؤلاء البغداديين، يَرُدَّ هذه الدعوى الاستشراقية، القائمة على التخمين فحسب .
And his book which he named 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Basriyya' concerning issues that arose between him and the Mu'tazila of Basra, and similarly the book 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Baghdadiyya' concerning issues that arose with the Baghdadis among them. Some orientalists claim that he feared them and flattered them, and that he changed some of his statements to agree with them. But this book, together with the direct narratives of Ibn Khafif in the book 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir' about his heated confrontations with these Baghdadis, refutes this orientalist allegation, which is based on mere conjecture.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage introduces two works by al-Ash'ari: the 'Scattered Issues of Basra' and the 'Scattered Issues of Baghdad', collections of disputations with Mu'tazili scholars from those cities. The author then addresses an orientalist claim that al-Ash'ari was intimidated by the Baghdad Mu'tazila and altered his views to appease them. The author argues that these very books, along with the reports of Ibn Khafif about al-Ash'ari's vigorous debates, disprove that claim. The passage thus serves both to list the works and to defend al-Ash'ari's intellectual independence.

Refuting Orientalist Claims about al-Ash'ari
Refutation of orientalist claim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari's writings and Ibn Khafif's accounts refute the orientalist claim that al-Ash'ari feared and flattered the Baghdad Mu'tazila.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's books prove he debated Mu'tazila boldly, not fearfully.

Some orientalists have suggested that al-Ash'ari was intimidated by the Mu'tazila of Baghdad and altered his views to please them. This lesson examines the evidence that refutes this claim, drawn directly from his own works and contemporary sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the orientalist claim
The claim is that al-Ash'ari feared and flattered the Baghdad Mu'tazila, even changing his statements to agree with them.
2
Examine the first piece of evidence
The passage states that the very book 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura' refutes this claim. It contains the actual debates.
3
Consider the second piece of evidence
Ibn Khafif's 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir' recounts heated confrontations between al-Ash'ari and the Baghdadis.
4
Conclude the refutation
The orientalist allegation is dismissed as based on conjecture, not evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكتابه الذي أسماه : المسائل المنثورة البصرية»، في مسائل أثيرت ت بينه وبين معتزلة البصرة، ومثله كتاب المسائل المنثورة البغدادية» في مسائل أُثيرَتْ مع البغداديين منهم، الذين يزعم بعضُ المستشرقين أنه كان يخافهم ويجاملهم، وأنه غير بعض أقواله لِيُوافِقَهم، وهذا الكتاب مع الروايات المباشرة لابن خفيف -في كتاب سيرة الشيخ الكبير عن مواجهاته المحتَدِمَةِ مع هؤلاء البغداديين، يَرُدَّ هذه الدعوى الاستشراقية، القائمة على التخمين فحسب .
And his book which he named 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Basriyya' concerning issues that arose between him and the Mu'tazila of Basra, and similarly the book 'al-Masa'il al-Manthura al-Baghdadiyya' concerning issues that arose with the Baghdadis among them. Some orientalists claim that he feared them and flattered them, and that he changed some of his statements to agree with them. But this book, together with the direct narratives of Ibn Khafif in the book 'Sirat al-Shaykh al-Kabir' about his heated confrontations with these Baghdadis, refutes this orientalist allegation, which is based on mere conjecture.

Commentary
This passage introduces two works by al-Ash'ari: the 'Scattered Issues of Basra' and the 'Scattered Issues of Baghdad', collections of disputations with Mu'tazili scholars from those cities. The author then addresses an orientalist claim that al-Ash'ari was intimidated by the Baghdad Mu'tazila and altered his views to appease them. The author argues that these very books, along with the reports of Ibn Khafif about al-Ash'ari's vigorous debates, disprove that claim. The passage thus serves both to list the works and to defend al-Ash'ari's intellectual independence.

Al-Ash'ari's Works Refuting Philosophers and the Theory of Emanation
List of al-Ash'ari's works against philosophers and others.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the breadth of al-Ash'ari's engagement with philosophical schools, including his early critique of the theory of emanation.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari directly refuted Aristotle, dualists, and astrological determinism.

This passage from biographical literature lists several of al-Ash'ari's polemical works. It shows that he was deeply engaged with contemporary philosophical and theological debates, refuting not only Muslim innovators but also Christians, dualists, and Greek philosophers like Aristotle. Notably, it includes an early critique of the theory of emanation later systematized by al-Farabi.

Guided Path
1

Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the books mentioned.
Notice that the passage distinguishes between different types of opponents.
2
Identify the groups refuted
Note the specific groups: later scholars (muhdathin), Christians (Nasara), dualists, and philosophers (including Aristotle).
Al-Ash'ari's refutations cover a wide range of intellectual currents.
3
Focus on the philosophical refutations
Pay special attention to the books against philosophers and the description of the 'Refutation of the Philosophers' with its three articles.
The passage names specific philosophical concepts like hyle and natures.
4
Understand the theory of emanation
Understand that the passage identifies al-Ash'ari as an early critic of the emanation theory, which al-Farabi later introduced into Islamic thought.
This shows al-Ash'ari's awareness of pre-Islamic and contemporary philosophical ideas.

وكتاب «الفنون» في الرد على بعض المحدثين، وهو غير الفنون في علم الكلام السابق ذكره . (۱) ابن عساکر تبیین کذب المفتري، ۱۳۲. وكتاب: المسائل على أهل التثنية»، «فيه الكلام على النصارى - ومن ثلث فقد ثنّى وعدد». قال عنه ابن فورك : إنه يحتج عليهم فيه من الكتب التي يعتدون بها (۱) . وآخر مثله في بيان مذهب النصارى. وله عدة كتب في مناقشة أقوال الفلاسفة، منها : «نقض كتاب الآثار العلوية لأرسطو، وهذا الكتاب وأشباهه، يردُّ مقالة شيخنا الدكتور غرابة في عدم إلمام الشيخ بالمقالات الفلسفية (٢) - وكتاب في مناقشة مقالات الفلاسفة»، بوجه عام. - وكتاب في الرد على الفلاسفة»، قال عنه الأشعري إنه يشتمل على ثلاث مقالات : ذكرنا فيها نقض علل ابن قيس الدهري - وأحسبه يقصد الفيلسوف أيرقلس وتكلمنا فيه على القائلين بالهيولى والطبائع، ونقضنا فيه علل أرسطوطاليس في والعالم، وبينا ما عليهم في قولهم بإضافة الأحداث إلى النجوم، وتعليق أحكام السعادة والشقاوة بها، وهو نقد مبكر لنظرية الفيض ) (۳) التي أدخلها الفارابي في الفكر الفلسفي الإسلامي.
And the book 'al-Funun' in refutation of some later scholars (muhdathin), and it is not the 'al-Funun' in kalam previously mentioned. (1) Ibn 'Asakir, Tabyin Kadhib al-Muftari, p. 132. And the book 'al-Masa'il 'ala Ahl al-Tathniya', 'in which is speech against the Christians - 'and whoever thirds has indeed doubled and numbered.' Ibn Furak said about it: 'He argues against them from the books they consider authoritative.' And another similar one expounding the doctrine of the Christians. And he has several books discussing the statements of the philosophers, among them: 'Refutation of the Book of the Supernal Effects of Aristotle' - this book and its like refute the statement of our teacher Dr. Gharaba about the Sheikh's lack of familiarity with philosophical articles (2) - and a book 'Discussions of the Articles of the Philosophers' in general. And a book 'Refutation of the Philosophers', about which al-Ash'ari said it contains three articles: 'We mentioned in them the refutation of the causes of Ibn Qays al-Dahri - and I think he means the philosopher Hierocles - and we spoke in it against those who assert hyle (hayula) and natures (taba'i'), and we refuted in it the causes of Aristotle concerning the heavens and the world, and we made clear what they are liable for in their statement of attributing events to the stars and the attachment of the judgments of happiness and misery to them, and it is an early critique of the theory of emanation (al-fayd) which al-Farabi introduced into Islamic philosophical thought.'
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage continues listing al-Ash'ari's works. First, 'al-Funun' refutes some later scholars, distinct from another book with the same name on kalam. Then there is a footnote to Ibn 'Asakir. Next, a book against the dualists (Christians) where al-Ash'ari uses their own scriptures. Then a similar exposition of Christian doctrine. The main part lists works against philosophers: a refutation of Aristotle's 'On the Heavens', which also rebuts the modern claim that al-Ash'ari was not versed in philosophy. Another general book on philosophical articles. Finally, a three-article refutation of philosophers including Ibn Qays al-Dahri (probably Hierocles), those who believe in hyle and natures, Aristotle's arguments on the heavens, and astrological claims. The author notes this is an early criticism of the emanation theory later championed by al-Farabi.

Imam al-Ash'ari's Polemical Works
Editor lists Ash'ari's book al-Luma and his works against dualists and Christians.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the method and scope of Imam al-Ash'ari's refutations of dualists and Christians through his key works.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari used his opponents' own scriptures to argue against them.

This lesson introduces two key works of Imam al-Ash'ari that demonstrate his method of engaging with deviant sects. The passage highlights his refutation of dualists and Christians, using arguments from their own authoritative texts. It also includes a remark by Ibn Furak on Ash'ari's strategy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then its full translation. Notice the titles of the works and the quoted phrase.
The phrase 'man thallatha faqad thanna wa 'addad' is a key argument against trinitarian doctrine.
2
Identify the three works mentioned
The editor lists three items: al-Luma', a book on dualists (which includes refutation of Christians), and another similar work on Christianity. Note how they form a cohesive polemical project.
3
Reflect on the quoted argument
The phrase 'whoever thirds has dualized and numbered' means that dividing the divine into three persons is tantamount to dualism (tathniya) and implies multiplicity—contradicting tawhid.
This reflects early kalām arguments against Christian trinitarianism.
4
Understand Ibn Furak's comment
Ibn Furak highlights that Ash'ari argued against Christians using their own authoritative texts, showing his scholarly method of internal critique.
This underlines the importance of knowing opponents' scriptures for effective refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اللُّمَع في الردّ على أَهلِ الزَّيْغِ والبِدَع. وكتاب: المسائل على أهل التثنية، فيه الكلام على النصارى - ومن ثلث فقد ثنّى وعدد. قال عنه ابن فورك : إنه يحتج عليهم فيه من الكتب التي يعتدون بها. وآخر مثله في بيان مذهب النصارى.
Al-Luma' in refutation of the people of deviation and innovation. And the book: 'Issues on the People of Duality', in it is discourse on the Christians - 'and whoever thirds has dualized and numbered'. Ibn Furak said about it: He argues against them in it from the books they consider authoritative. And another similar [book] on clarifying the doctrine of the Christians.

Commentary
This passage is a listing by the editor of Imam al-Ash'ari's works. It begins with the book title 'Al-Luma' fi al-Radd 'ala Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Bida''. Then it mentions a specific book titled 'Al-Masa'il 'ala Ahl al-Tathniya' about dualists, which includes a discussion on Christians. The phrase 'man thallatha faqad thanna wa 'addad' is quoted, meaning that whoever posits a third (trinity) has effectively dualized and counted (i.e., engaged in numerical multiplicity). Ibn Furak is cited stating that al-Ash'ari uses scriptures that the Christians themselves accept to argue against them. The passage ends noting another similar work on exposing the Christian doctrine.

Al-Ash'ari's Refutations of Philosophers
Editor lists al-Ash'ari's works refuting philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Imam al-Ash'ari wrote detailed refutations of Greek philosophers and the Neoplatonic theory of emanation, contrary to claims that he was unfamiliar with philosophical discourse.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari engaged deeply with philosophy to refute it from an Islamic perspective.

This passage from the editor of al-Luma' lists several works by Imam al-Ash'ari dedicated to refuting philosophers. It shows that al-Ash'ari was not only aware of Greek philosophical ideas but also wrote systematic critiques, including an early refutation of the theory of emanation introduced by al-Farabi. This directly counters the misconception that al-Ash'ari was ignorant of philosophy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Identify the three books mentioned and their contents.
2
List the philosophical targets
The passage mentions specific philosophers and ideas: Aristotle, Ibn Qays al-Dahri (Heraclitus), proponents of hyle and natures, and the theory of emanation. Make a note of each.
3
Understand the significance
Al-Ash'ari's refutations demonstrate his deep knowledge of Greek and Neoplatonic philosophy. This directly refutes claims that he was unaware of philosophical arguments.
4
Connect to Islamic thought
Note that al-Ash'ari's critique of the theory of emanation came before al-Farabi's full elaboration, showing that Islamic theology was already engaging with Neoplatonism early on.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وله عدة كتب في مناقشة أقوال الفلاسفة، منها : «نقض كتاب الآثار العلوية لأرسطو، وهذا الكتاب وأشباهه، يردُّ مقالة شيخنا الدكتور غرابة في عدم إلمام الشيخ بالمقالات الفلسفية. وكتاب في مناقشة مقالات الفلاسفة، بوجه عام. وكتاب في الرد على الفلاسفة، قال عنه الأشعري إنه يشتمل على ثلاث مقالات : ذكرنا فيها نقض علل ابن قيس الدهري - وأحسبه يقصد الفيلسوف أيرقلس وتكلمنا فيه على القائلين بالهيولى والطبائع، ونقضنا فيه علل أرسطوطاليس في والعالم، وبينا ما عليهم في قولهم بإضافة الأحداث إلى النجوم، وتعليق أحكام السعادة والشقاوة بها، وهو نقد مبكر لنظرية الفيض التي أدخلها الفارابي في الفكر الفلسفي الإسلامي.
And he has several books on debating the sayings of the philosophers, including: 'Refutation of the Book of Celestial Effects of Aristotle' – and this book and its like refute the statement of our shaykh Dr. Gharaba regarding the shaykh's [al-Ash'ari's] lack of familiarity with philosophical discourses. And a book on debating the articles of the philosophers in general. And a book on refuting the philosophers, about which al-Ash'ari said: It comprises three articles in which we mentioned the refutation of the causes of Ibn Qays al-Dahri – and I think he means the philosopher Heraclitus – and we discussed therein the proponents of hyle and natures, and we refuted therein the causes of Aristotle concerning [؟] the world, and we made clear their error in their statement of attributing events to the stars, and hanging judgments of happiness and misery on them. And it is an early critique of the theory of emanation which al-Farabi introduced into Islamic philosophical thought.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage lists al-Ash'ari's works refuting philosophers. The editor first mentions 'Naqd Kitab al-Athar al-'Uluwiyya li-Aristu' (Refutation of Aristotle's Book of Celestial Effects), noting that this work refutes Dr. Gharaba's claim that al-Ash'ari was unfamiliar with philosophy. Then there is a general work refuting the philosophers' articles. Third, a book specifically titled 'Fi al-Radd 'ala al-Falasifa', which al-Ash'ari himself described as containing three articles: refuting the causal theories of 'Ibn Qays al-Dahri' (likely Heraclitus), discussing the proponents of hyle (matter) and natures (materialists/physicalists), refuting Aristotle's arguments about the world, and criticizing the astrological attribution of events and judgments to stars. The editor notes this is an early critique of the Neoplatonic theory of emanation brought into Islamic philosophy by al-Farabi.

Al-Ash'ari's book on reincarnation defended core Islamic beliefs about the afterlife.

This brief mention from the editor introduces one of al-Ash'ari's works dedicated to debating the proponents of reincarnation (tanasukh). Editorial Defense of al-Ash'ari's Philosophical Knowledge
Editor argues that al-Ash'ari's four books refute doubts about his philosophical knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the editor's argument that al-Ash'ari's own works demonstrate his engagement with philosophy, contrary to claims that only later Ash'aris did so.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari's four books refute claims that he was uninvolved with philosophy.

This passage features the editor of al-Luma defending al-Ash'ari against modern scholarly doubts. The editor points to four of al-Ash'ari's works as direct evidence of his engagement with philosophical questions, and cites Muhammad Iqbal's broader assessment of Ash'arism as an Islamic revolution against Greek thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim being refuted
Notice that the editor is responding to Dr. Gharaba's doubt about al-Ash'ari's knowledge of philosophy. Understand what the doubt claims.
Gharaba suggested that only later Ash'aris engaged with philosophy.
2
Examine the evidence: four books
The editor states that four specific works by al-Ash'ari refute this doubt. Consider what these books might cover.
These books are likely those mentioned earlier in the original lesson.
3
Recognize the three philosophical issues
The passage lists three classic issues: divine science (al-ilm al-ilahi), eternity of the world (qidam al-alam), and resurrection (al-ma'ad). These were central to the Ash'ari critique of philosophy.
4
Consider Iqbal's interpretation
Muhammad Iqbal argued that Ash'ari efforts constitute a revolution of Islamic thought against Greek ideas. Think about how this supports the editor's defense.
Iqbal's view frames Ash'arism as a proactive intellectual movement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذه المؤلفات الأربعة الأخيرة تَرُدُّ على تساؤل شيخنا د. غرابة : عن مدى معرفة الشيخ بالمقولات الفلسفية، واستبعاده هو ذلك، وأن أتباعه المتأخرين هم الذين ناقشوا ما أثاره الفلاسفة، من المشائين وغيرهم حول قدم العالم، وسائر المسائل الثلاث التي أخذها عليهم الأشاعرة وخصوصا الغزالي- في العلم الإلهي، وقدم العَالِمَ ، والمعاد. وقد كان محمد إقبال» (۱۹۳۸م) أقرب إلى الصحة؛ إذ قال : إن جهود الأشاعرة وأقوالهم تشبه أن تكون ثورة - من جانب الفكر الإسلامي - على الآراء الإغريقية بوجه عام، وفي تفسير العالم والطبيعة بوجه خاص.
And these last four works refute the question of our shaykh Dr. Gharaba: about the extent of the shaykh's [al-Ash'ari's] knowledge of philosophical categories, and his exclusion of that, and that his later followers are the ones who discussed what the philosophers, Peripatetics and others, raised about the eternity of the world, and the rest of the three issues that the Ash'aris, especially al-Ghazali, criticized them on – in divine knowledge, the eternity of the world [؟], and the resurrection. And Muhammad Iqbal (1938 CE) was closer to correctness; he said: The efforts and sayings of the Ash'aris resemble a revolution – from the side of Islamic thought – against Greek views in general, and in the interpretation of the world and nature in particular.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is the editor's argument that the four previously mentioned books (against philosophers, reincarnation, etc.) refute Dr. Gharaba's claim that al-Ash'ari was unfamiliar with philosophy and his later followers were the ones who engaged with philosophical issues like the eternity of the world, the three classic issues (divine science, eternity of the world, resurrection) highlighted by al-Ghazali. The editor then cites Muhammad Iqbal's view that Ash'ari efforts represent an Islamic revolution against Greek thought in cosmology and natural philosophy.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Iqbal described the Ash'ari effort as an 'intellectual revolution'. Where in your own understanding of Islam do you need a similar revolution—a thorough rethinking of your assumptions about the world and nature?

Al-Ash'ari's Self-Critique: Refuting His Own Past
Editor describes al-Ash'ari's self-refuting book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ash'ari's practice of self-critique through his book 'Al-Jawabat fi al-Sifat', in which he refuted his earlier Mu'tazilite work.

Core Idea
Al-Ash'ari wrote to refute his own past Mu'tazilite writings.

After his conversion from Mu'tazilism, Imam al-Ash'ari not only refuted the doctrines of others but also critically examined his own earlier works. One notable example is his book 'Al-Jawabat fi al-Sifat', which he wrote to overturn a previous book he had authored in support of Mu'tazilite views. This lesson examines that self-refuting effort.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the editorial framing and the direct quote from al-Ash'ari.
The Arabic contains OCR issues; focus on the intended meaning.
2
Understand the context of self-critique
Consider why a scholar would write a book refuting his own earlier work. Reflect on al-Ash'ari's motivation: fear that his previous views might be attributed to him.
3
Reflect on scholarly integrity
Think about the significance of publicly correcting one's own errors. This demonstrates intellectual honesty and commitment to truth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القسم الثالث والأخير من الكتب النقدية «الذاتية»، وهو الله - ردوده -رحمه على نفسه؛ خشية أن تلصق به آراؤُه ومواقفه السابقة، والذائعة عنه، عنه ، في أيام الاعتزال فمنها : - كتاب «الجوابات في الصفات عن مسائل أهل الزيغ والشبهات ، يقول عنه : نقضنا فيه كتاباً ، كنَّا ألفناه قديما فيها ، على تصحيح مذهب المعتزلة ، لم يؤلّف لهم مثله ، ثم أبان الله سبحانه لنا
As for the third and final section of the critical 'self-refuting' books – and it is God [؟] – his responses – may God have mercy on him – on himself; fearing that his previous views and positions that were famous about him might be attributed to him, from his days of I'tizal. Among them: The book 'Al-Jawabat fi al-Sifat 'an Masa'il Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Shubuhat', he says about it: Therein we refuted a book we had previously authored, on correcting the Mu'tazilite doctrine, of which no like had been authored for them, then Allah – exalted is He – showed us...
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage introduces the third category of al-Ash'ari's critical works: those that he wrote to refute his own earlier Mu'tazilite positions. The editor comments that al-Ash'ari feared his previous views might be attributed to him, so he wrote a refutation. The specific book mentioned is 'Al-Jawabat fi al-Sifat 'an Masa'il Ahl al-Zaygh wa al-Shubuhat' (The Responses on the Attributes Concerning Questions of the People of Deviation and Doubts). Al-Ash'ari states that in this book he refuted a previous book he had written in support of Mu'tazilism, which had no parallel in its defense of their doctrine. Then Allah guided him to the truth.

Misconception: Al-Ash'ari remained a Mu'tazili throughout his life.
Correction: This passage shows that al-Ash'ari actively refuted his own earlier Mu'tazilite writings, demonstrating his departure from that school.

B) To refute a book he previously wrote supporting Mu'tazilism.
C) To explain the attributes of God in detail.
D) To respond to Christian criticisms.

Key Takeaway
Al-Ash'ari's book 'Al-Jawabat fi al-Sifat' exemplifies his self-critical approach, as he publicly refuted his own earlier Mu'tazilite work out of fear that his past views would be attributed to him.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
Al-Ash'ari feared his past Mu'tazilite views would be attributed to him. Are there any past views or actions of yours that you fear might define you in the eyes of others? What are you doing to correct that?
?
Al-Ash'ari wrote a book that had no parallel in defending a false doctrine, then refuted it. Have you ever invested significant effort in something only to later realize it was misguided? How would you respond if you had to publicly undo that work?

Ash'ari's Retracted Book and Lost Works
Editor notes Ash'ari's retraction of a book and describes his lost epistolary works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Imam al-Ash'ari retracted one of his books and what kinds of his written and oral works have been lost.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's intellectual humility: he retracted his own book and warned against relying on it.

This passage from an editor's commentary gives us a glimpse into the breadth of Imam al-Ash'ari's scholarly output and his integrity. We learn that he wrote a book on a particular topic and later retracted it, showing his willingness to correct himself. The editor also describes the extensive correspondence and dictation sessions that have unfortunately been lost, though some manuscripts have recently surfaced.

Guided Path
1
Read about the retracted book
Read the Arabic passage and translation focusing on the book on 'thing' and Ash'ari's retraction. Notice his explicit warning not to rely on it.
This shows his scholarly honesty.
2

The passage describes the fourth category of Ash'ari's writings: his epistolary responses to scholars. Understand that these were written answers to creedal questions from across the Islamic world.
These responses were similar to his oral debates.
3

Consider why so many works were lost and how the recent discovery of manuscripts renews hope for future recovery.
Large volumes disappeared, so smaller letters are also gone.
