⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها كتابه في باب شيء، وأن الأشياء هي أشياء وإن عدمن، قال عنه أيضًا: رجعنا عنه، ونقضناه، فمن وقع إليه فلا يعول عليه. هما: بقي ومجالسه الآن ضربان من أضرب التأليف لدى هذا القلم السيال، ٤ - النوع الرابع من المؤلفات المتمثل في: رسائله الجوابية على أسئلة علماء الأمصار والبلاد الإسلامية في المشرق والمغرب، حول مسائل العقيدة وهي تُماثِلُ الجوابات الشفوية، في مجلس الجدال بالبصرة وبغداد ومثلُهما أيضًا إملاءاتُه مع أصحابه وتلاميذه في هاتين المدينتين العامرتين، وهو نشاط لا يمكن إحصاؤه، لفت أنظار العلماء فرحلوا إليه، وجلسوا بين يديه، أو استمعوا لمناقشاته وحواراته الجدلية التي لم تسجل للأسف الشديد؛ بل إن الجوابات والردود المكتوبة والمجالس المملاة كانت أحرى لتدوينها بالكتابة بالبقاء والنقل، ولكنا حتى الآن لم نعثر على أي منهما، وإن وردت إشارات إلى نحو ذلك، في بعض مؤلفاته، حيث يقول: وقلنا، وألزمناهم، وسألناهم ونحوها. وإذا كانت الكتب الكبيرة، والمجلدات العديدة قد اختفت أو أبيدت، فلا عجب في اختفاء الرسائل والأمالي، والمجالس والمناظرات. ولا حول ولا قوة إلا بالله... لكن ظهور بعض المخطوطات أخيرا له، ولتلاميذه على ندرتها - يجدِّدُ أملنا، ويقوي عزمنا على مواصلة البحث والتّحرّي، عن هذه الكنوز الفكرية المفقودة.
And among them is his book on the chapter of 'thing', and that things are things even if they cease to exist. He also said about it: 'We retracted it, and we refuted it, so whoever comes across it should not rely on it.' There remain: his sessions now are two types of authorship by this flowing pen: 4 - The fourth type of writings represented in his epistolary responses to questions of scholars of the regions and Islamic lands in the East and the West, concerning matters of creed. And they resemble the oral responses in the debating sessions in Basra and Baghdad, and likewise his dictations with his companions and students in these two flourishing cities. And it is an activity that cannot be counted; it attracted the attention of scholars so they traveled to him and sat before him, or listened to his debates and disputations, which unfortunately were not recorded. But rather the written responses and replies and the dictated sessions were more deserving of being recorded in writing for preservation and transmission, but we have not found any of them until now, although there are indications of that in some of his works, where he says: 'We said, and we compelled them, and we asked them' and the like. And if the large books and numerous volumes have disappeared or been destroyed, there is no wonder at the disappearance of the epistles, dictations, sessions, and debates. There is no power and no strength except with God. However, the recent appearance of some manuscripts of his and of his students, despite their rarity, renews our hope and strengthens our resolve to continue research and investigation for these lost intellectual treasures.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage is an editorial note describing two aspects of Imam al-Ash'ari's literary output. First, it mentions that Ash'ari wrote a book on the topic of 'thing' (i.e., the ontological status of things), and that he later retracted it, warning people not to rely on it. This shows Ash'ari's willingness to correct his own views. Second, the editor introduces the fourth category of Ash'ari's writings: his epistolary responses to scholars from various Islamic regions on creedal questions. The editor notes that these responses were akin to his oral debates in Basra and Baghdad, and that he also had dictation sessions with his students. Unfortunately, almost all of these works have been lost. The editor laments that even the larger works have disappeared, so the loss of smaller epistles is unsurprising. However, the recent discovery of some manuscripts gives hope for future recovery.

إملاءاتُه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Ash'ari's retracted book represents his final view, but he explicitly warned against relying on it.
Correction: Ash'ari himself said he retracted and refuted it, so it should not be considered part of his mature theology.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Ash'ari retracted a book on the nature of things and warned against using it, while his extensive epistolary and dictation works are largely lost but recently rediscovered manuscripts offer hope.

?
Scholars traveled great distances to sit before Ash'ari. Have you made any real sacrifice—time, comfort, or effort—to seek knowledge from those who embody it? If not, what is holding you back?

Ash'ari's Humble Beginnings and Global Reach
Editor enumerates regions and marvels at Ash'ari's productivity despite poverty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Ash'ari's humble circumstances did not hinder his vast scholarly output and widespread influence.

Core Idea
Poverty and orphanhood could not stop Ash'ari's scholarship from reaching the Islamic world.

This passage is an editor's reflection on the remarkable scale of Ash'ari's correspondence. Despite being an orphan living on a meager annual income of just seventeen dirhams, his works reached regions across the Islamic world. It is a powerful reminder that material limitations need not constrain intellectual impact.

The editor explicitly marvels at how such a man could achieve so much. This is meant to inspire the reader.

وضمن هذا القسم المتعلق بجواباته لما ورد إليه من أكثر الأمصار الإسلامية: نجد مصر وغيرها بعنوان جواب المصريين في مسائل من الكلام... وكتاب الطبرانيين، والخراسانيين، والأرجانيين، والشبراطيين والعمانيين، والجُرجانيين، والدمشقيين والواسطيين، والرامهرمزيين وغيرهم. وإن المرء ليعجب كيف تسنّى لرجل نشأ يتيمًا، وعاش فقيرًا وحيدا زاهدًا، ينفق، من ريع وقف لأحد آبائه ما قيمته سبعة عشر درهما في كل عام، وقد وفد عليه ابن خفيف في البصرة، وصحبه مرة إلى بيته، بحي منها، ولكنه لم يذكر لنا شيئًا عن أهل أو ولد - أقول: كيف تسنى لأبي الحسن في ظل هذه الظروف أن يُصنف هذه التصانيف في علوم شتى ومجالات متنوعة، وكيف ذاع صيته حتى بلغ إلى الأقطار الإسلامية كافة، حتى جاءته الرسائل تحمل المسائل.

Commentary
This passage is an editorial reflection on the scale of Imam al-Ash'ari's correspondence and his remarkable productivity. The editor lists several regions from which Ash'ari received questions: Egypt, Tabaristan, Khurasan, Arjan, Shibrat, Oman, Jurjan, Damascus, Wasit, and Ramhurmuz. This indicates the wide geographical reach of his influence. Then the editor expresses astonishment that Ash'ari, despite being an orphan living in poverty with an annual income of only seventeen dirhams from an ancestral endowment, managed to produce such a vast corpus of writings across many sciences. The editor mentions that the Sufi Ibn Khafif visited him and saw his humble home, and that Ash'ari had no family or children mentioned. The editor concludes by marveling that Ash'ari's fame spread across the entire Islamic world, with letters bringing questions from far and wide.

Editorial reflection on lost works and list of regions Ash'ari responded to

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that despite the loss of many of Ash'ari's works, manuscript discoveries continue to renew hope, and that his responses reached a wide geographic range across the Islamic world.

Core Idea
Ash'ari's responses spanned the Islamic world, and lost manuscripts still surface today.

This editorial passage from the introduction to al-Luma' reflects on the tragic loss of many of Ash'ari's works, yet also gives hope through recent manuscript discoveries. It also provides a fascinating glimpse into the wide geographic reach of Ash'ari's theological influence, listing regions from Egypt to Khurasan.

Commentary
This passage is an editorial commentary from the introduction (مقدمة التحقيق). It begins by noting that large books and volumes have disappeared, so it is not surprising that smaller treatises (رسائل), dictations (أمالي), sessions (مجالس), and debates (مناظرات) have also vanished. However, the recent appearance of some manuscripts of Ash'ari and his students renews hope. Then it mentions that within the section of Ash'ari's responses to questions from various Islamic regions, we find responses to Egypt and many other regions listed by their nisbas: Tabaraniyyun, Khurasaniyyun, Arjaniyyun, Shibratiyyun, Umaniyyun, Jurjaniyyun, Dimashqiyyun, Wasitiyyun, Ramhurmuziyyun, and others.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The editor finds hope in the rediscovery of lost manuscripts. Think of something spiritually valuable that you have neglected or lost in your own life. What is one specific action you can take this week to reconnect with that treasure?
?
Al-Ash'ari answered questions from communities as far as Oman and Khurasan. How often do you consider the global brotherhood of Muslims beyond your locality? What is one concrete step you can take to learn from or support a Muslim community outside your region?
?
Large books and volumes have perished, yet fragments survive. If your own deeds and knowledge were to be 'rediscovered' after a long period, what would they reveal about your commitment to truth? What will you change today to ensure they reflect sincerity?
